Tilak thought, ‘For the progress and uplift of the country, the visit of the foreign countries should be made to know the secret of their progress. If the permission is granted by the old Pandits for the visit of the foreign countries, the moral hurdle will be over.

With this consideration Mahamanya Tilak reached Kashi and there he requested a Mahamahopadhyay ‘It will be much better if he certifies that with my sea-voyage there would be no harm to religion.’

Panditji heard the request of Tilak. He considered it a good opportunity. It is a good chance to charge money from Tilak. He had been serving his purpose of self-interest behind the curtain of religion some times in the past also. Now again, the greed of money flashed before his eyes. Giving the solution of the problems he said—

‘This journey is against the ethics of religion. In general condition we don’t allow anybody; but if you can spend rupees five thousand as atonement, you may be permitted to visit abroad under the religious sanctity. Tell me, can you manage this amount?’

Tilak was adamant to go abroad on any condition. He could manage this amount very easily. His economic condition was also better. Having managed the money when he thought to give the money, suddenly his innerself jolted him and the inner voice shook him off —

‘Religion is the ordain of God. Morality is the strong base of our society. If the moral wisdom is disregarded in this way, the moral system of the society will be shattered badly. I should not do this immoral act in my self-interest.

His unconscious mind began to curse him again and again for doing this act against the moral wisdom. His moral consciousness began to reproach him for changing the religion in his favour with the support of money. He began to feel his act improper. His innerself began to imprecate him for his conduct against morality. He could not pacify his moral wisdom.

At last, he decided—‘I will not allow immorality and self interest to dominate myself. I will not allow morality to be stigmatised by money. He turned back with the money. He did not defy the morality and he felt a great peace in his hidden mind.

The service of humanity is the best religion

‘Swami Ram Krishna Math’ had already been established in Calcutta. All of his devotees had already taken the enterance in the ‘Mutth’ having taken renunciation. The financial expenses of the ‘Mutth’ were met by the profit of the land attached to the ‘Mutth’. The hermits had no other work except devotional muttering, song and worship.

In the meantime by chance, plague broke out in Calcutta.

People in number began to suffer from this disease and die. Swami Vivekanand could not tolerate it and changed this religious Mutth into relief camp. He engaged all the spiritual priests in the service of the afflicted ones and said—

‘Brothers! The form of religion is changing today. The Lord has put his true devotees and hermits to test. The struggle between humanity and epidemic has broken out today. Today every hermit of the Mutth has to appear at the test and he has to present the proof of his truthfulness. The treatment and service of the patients, orphans, crippled, weak and helpless is the part of religion. Treat and serve the patients so much, be so compassionate to them that no patient of the ‘Mutth’ may be overtaken by the death. In case, there is shortage of money, I will sell the land of the ‘Mutth’. Don’t worry! Service is the religious work. The service of the patients is the service of the Lord.

On the influential call of Swami Vivekanand all the renunciates of the ‘Mutth’ engaged themselves in the service of the patients as if they were doing a divine work.

Knowledge, devotion and wisdom is needed and not money

Swami Vivekanand’s (the then Narendra) father earned money in abundance but all soon, spent. The result was that when he died, the economic condition of the family had been in dole-drums and it became difficult even to pull on livlihood.

Swamiji (Narendra) had passed B.A already at that time, but unfortunately he could get no job even after making great efforts. His mother and younger brothers and sisters reached the edge of starvation.

Even after graduation there was the financial problem. They were running through a very horrible condition. They were helpless to find out any way. No way out was visible.

Ultimately, being compelled and disturbed, he went to his guru (the preceptor) Shri Ramkrishna Paramhansji and narrated the pathetic condition of his financial stringency.

Shri Ramkrishna paramhansji thought over seriously. Then, he said—

‘You will get anything today whatever you demand from ‘Kalimata’ because your devotion is sincere. Strength lies in faith. The true devotion is always fruitful. Go, and demand.’

Swami Vivekanand was worried. What the helplessness not compells to do! The hungry man happens to do otherwise, even generally he forgets the discrimination of moral and immoral.

Swamiji’s devotion was certainly unswerving. After midnight he went to the temple of Goddess ‘Kalimata’ for the demand of money. Oh! What happened! What a change! Now, the situation is, he is standing with folded hands and forgot suddenly what he wanted to say.

Having forgotten his worldly interest he began to speak the words—

‘Mother! I want nothing. Bless me with only knowledge! Bless me with devotion! Bless me with wisdom and sentiment of detachment from the worldly affairs!’

Shri Ramkrishnaji was feeling astonished at his prayer. Why does he not demand money to get rid of starvation? He again sent him to the Mother Kali.

Not only once, but he sent him thrice to make his demand by assuring him fully that his demand would be fulfilled by the Mother.

But do you know what happened? Swami Vivekanand could not put the demand of money before the ‘Mata’ even a single time.

To wipe away the ignorance from the world is also a big pious act

By the grace of his Guru (preceptor) Swami Vivekanand had already acquired the self-realization along with the vision of the Lord. In a garden of Kashipur he was attending his guru (preceptor).

Just after attaining knowledge a thought flashed in the mind of Swamiji—

I will pass my whole life in spiritual practice in seclusion enjoying the Supreme Bliss in a trance renouncing the world.’

The inner dweller of all beings Guru intuited it and said—

‘Vivekanand! Your selfish spiritual outlook is not proper, you are not absolved of duty to free the world and the society from ignorance is also religion and now you have to accomplish this practical righteous work. You have yet not to enjoy the spiritual joy in seclusion. Now, create the moral awakening by your knowledege and wisdom.’

Now what was alternative for Vivekanandji?

He obeyed respectfully his Guru. He dedicated himself with his body and mind in the service of human beings instead of sitting alone in any solitary place absorbed in the Brahmic bliss.

Morality had saved from sin.

Mahatma Gandhi fell in a bad company in his childhood. The bad company is poisonous like epidemic disease. By falling into a bad company a man is often bent upon doing the evil deeds, which he will not do in his common life probably.

Young Gandhi reached such a polluted circumstance of evil thought, where he could commit sin like smoking, eating meat and sexual enjoyment with any other woman. His wicked friends took him to a prostitute by coaxing him. He was in a very critical situation. A common youth of general character would have certainly deviated from the right path to the downfall but abruptly Gandhiji’s moral sacred sacraments of his childhood knocked at his mind. His moral wisdom proved to be the shield in his protection.

Just as a strong branch cannot be twisted easily according to wish or the blots of the unripe earthen pots cannot be removed after being baked, the same way the moral sacraments of childhood cannot be wiped easily. Gandhiji had been taught since his childhood that smoking, eating meat and sexual enjoyment with another woman is a dreadful sin. A man should beaware of them.

Gandhiji’s innerself began to curse him from the inner side. As a result he was saved from the sin. The practice and teaching of moral conduct and sacraments saved him from the mud of sin of adultery.

The moral wisdom always keeps us cautions, that is the divine voice that always guides a man to the right path.

Consideration of others service

After being released from Ahamedabad jail, Pt. Nehru said while addressing a public meeting that he was about to visit Malaya in near future.

After his speech was over a slip was given to him. It was written in it—

‘My son is ill. The certain medicine is needed for his treatment . That medicine is not available anywhere except Malaya. You are to proceed for Malaya. If you may bring this medicine while coming back, it will be your great obligation.’

That man had noted down his complete address below it.

Whereas a great leader of a country like India and on the other side, a common man’s insistence to him to bring medicine. If there had been anyone else, he would have thrown away the slip folding it. But Nehruji considered the service of others as the practical part of religion. Whatever the service of others is possible by anyone, he should do it. The service of the patients, preceptors, weak, old and helpless is the religion. Even in his most busy and most important programmes of Malaya, Nehruji did not forget to bring that medicine and on the basis of the original slip, placed safely, coming back to India, he got the medicine sent to that patient.

Once, Pt. Nehru was going to Kamala Nehru hospital. On the way, his sight fell on the crippled female sweeper of his father’s time. That female sweeper had fondled Nehruji in her laps. At once, he got his car stopped and got down and running he embraced her to his neck. He began to ask her with choking throat, ‘O my Lachhminiyamai! How are you now?’ Overwhelmed by love, the female sweeper, having blessed him, burst to tears in emotion. Pt. Nehru had such high sense of close affinity, others distress and mentality of service that he had the consideration of everyone. He made the full arrangement of the female sweeper’s whole life.

This is the event of 1929—

At the time of Mahatma Gandhi’s country tour, Shri Prakashji and Pt. Nehru had stayed in a room of Masorrie. Suddenly Shri Prakashji felt headache. When Nehruji returned to his room being tired after the whole day work, he saw that Sri Prakashji was lying on the bed closing his eyes and the servant was rubbing his head.

Pandit Jawaharlal enquired of his condition. He got worried and with service and help point of view, after the walk of about one and half miles, he brought the tablets from the shop of a chemist to give him relief from the headache and made the patient Sri Prakashji to swallow the tablet. It lessened his pain and he could sleep comfortably.

In the same way in 1933 a member of Congress executive body, Shri Ram Saran felt headache. When Nehruji came to know it, he began to rub ointment on his head. In spite of the insistence to forbid, he remained rubbing his head till the patient fell asleep.

These occurences point out that there is practical side of the religion also which is useful in life at every step and at every moment. Religion is a practical life style. We should develop our soul and our virtues in the interest of the society. The virtues are tested at the time of distress. Even in the adverse circumstances and troublesome days let us remain holding the morality. This is the way of human evolution.

Man is the mine of virtues. The God is present in our soul. It is needed to make Him apparent by our day-to-day behaviour in our daily life. Let us be a great man and live righteousness in life, then, this world will become elegant. Morality makes us a good citizen. Divinity is sleeping in you. By the noble deeds, nobility and honesty awaken it and activate it. Live morality in your behaviour. Really, we need active morality. Winning over religion experience it.

 

They were one of them who are born but never die

From time to time among the human beings such great personalities have been flashing who can be called a diamond discovered in garbage. About these brightening diamonds the matter is usually noticed in the columns of newspapers. Here is being given some inspiring events of fragrant life-blossoms collected from different places which prove even today—‘कीर्तिर्यस्य स जीवति’, ‘They remain always alive who enjoy reputation.’ They were among these who are born, but never die.

1. I will not sell the priceless humanity for one hundred golden coins—

Once in a river of Italy such a flood occured that the entire bridge except a portion in the middle on which a house was situated, washed away. The afflicted family members of the house, peeping through the windows began to call the people standing on the border in the pathetic cry to protect their lives. The cracked part of the house was but to be washed away. The flood like the broadened jaws of the death was ready to swallow up the helpless.

...............Just to be flowed away! Just the end! just to drown, just to die!! Death............guffawing, a dreadful sight of death!!

The big rush of grieved viewers standing on the river bank was witnessing the pathetic sight. All and sundry wanted to save them, but one’s own life is dear to all. Who is there anyone to sacrifice one’s life for other’s one. What a selfish the world is!

In the meanwhile a rich man from the crowd feeling pity proclaimed loudly—

‘If anyone saves the men surrounded in trouble, I will give him one hundred gold coins in reward. Is there anyone such courageous to win this prize by saving the lives of these unfortunates from the flood?’

A poor man remained hearing. The feeling of benevolence was awakened in his mind.

The proclaimation was made again. It was proclaimed far and wide in a loud voice. He could not control himself.

The poor youth felt encouraged. He was a boatman, robust in body of irresistible boldness and zeal with the spirit of help of humanity, he reached the rest part of the river with his boat with indomitable courage and zeal without caring for the waves. The people were presuming to see his life in danger that he would also lose his life. The greed of reward will end his life from the world forever. The greed for money is blind.

But that courageous youth won. Facing hundreds of hardships, struggling against death and overcoming it, that brave, ultimately, brought the men in trouble safely to the bank again.

Now, all showered unreserved praises upon him. They were praising in exagerating words. The men escaped from the calamity were also bowing down to his obligation.

Then, that rich man began to give the reward of one hundred gold coins to that poor youth according to his proclaimation in the joyous mood. This was the understanding of the people that the poor youth would feel happy for his good fortune to get this big reward.

But what this!

That poor youth refused to accept that reward of one hundred golden coins.

The richman said hypocritically—‘You have saved the lives of these men from the jaws of death taking the risk of your own life. Every moment was dreadful for your life. You should accept your reward gladly, Take these one hundred gold coins. Count them whether they are exact in nuumber?’

Then, whatever the young boatman said is the treasure of humanity. All of us should feel proud of it even today.

He said—

‘I will not sell humanity by accepting one hundred gold coins. I have not saved these men in misery for the greed of money. Donate this amount among these helpless because their need is more important than mine.

It is truly said—

वस्यो भूयाय वसुमान् यज्ञो वसु वंशिषीय वसुमान् भूयासं वसु मयि धेहि॥

(Atharvaved 16/9/4)

‘O the mankind! Have full faith in God and in this world by practising the benevolence acquire the supreme abode. The capital of benevolence is the divine property, everlasting divine majesty. The benevolent remains happy in this world and after death he is always remembered.’

2. The imitable sacrifice of a widow—

There is an old Pakka well of one hundred and fifty years old on the road going from Mungyer to Bhagalpur. The well is named as the well of Shyamo Pisanhar near the well there are trees of Neem, Peepal and Gular, which cool shade has made a comfortable spot for the travellers to take rest. Long ago, a seventy years old lady named Shyamo had got it made. Her name still continues on the tongue of the people. The story runs as such—

When Shyamo was only 13 years old, within one year of her marriage she had become widow. She was insulted in her husband’s house and she was abused. She came back to her father. For sometimes, her parents remained alive but after their death the entire responsibility was thurst upon her. Shyamo thought—

‘The youth period will pass not by sitting idle but by doing labour and some work. To depend on the food earned by labour is man’s moral duty. So long as the limbs of the body are working, something must be done. Those only can remain steadfast in righteousness, who keep their body and mind engaged in some work. In the idle mind evil thoughts and passion keep revolving. There is always fear of going astray from the right path. I will earn the bread by manual labour and also do some benevolent deed also.

Well! This became her resolve. The God exists in the virtuous resolve.

She lived like an ascetic doing labour. The young widow got up two hours earlier in the night before the sun-rise and finished the grinding of five kg. flour till morning. Then, she worked on the water kiosk. Cutting the grass she sold it. Whatever the work was available to her, she used to do it earnestly. She cooked anybody’s food, sometimes she washed the clothes of someone or supported in cleaning. After taking some rest in the mid day, she again grinded the flour. After noon in the third part of the day she spinned the cotton threads on the spinning wheel. She developed the habit of labour. Whatever the work she got, she used to do it and thus, she remained collecting the money.

Throughout her life she earned five hundred rupees. She thought to invest it in some virtuous work. The place, where there is pitch road today, it was the rough road earlier. Water was no where to drink. The travellers felt a great difficulty in want of water. She spent the entire earning of her life in getting the Pakka well built. Those were the days of cheapness. In such a small amount that Pakka well was constructed. Even today that well reminds of that widow’s devotion to benevolence, hard labour, restraint and outstanding sacrifice.

Having an altruistic outlook can we not get any library, public inn or water kiosk etc., built?

The late Shyamo’s spirit gives the sermon of benevolence and generosity view. It may not attract the attention of others but she motivates that we should do the virutous acts in any situation wherever we stand; we should be charity-minded and we should never deviate from the moral path.

3. Her glory is spreading fragrance even today—

When, the Ambala passenger train passed through the culvert near Bhatinda, abruptly, the engine driver, Daulatram saw with opened eyes that the front culvert was damaged. If the train passed over it, it would cause a fierce accident and thousands of persons would die the death of flies. His heart was overwhelmed with humane pity and pathos. He could not bear this fierce train accident; but what should he do?

The violent dance of death was before his eye-sight. He was thinking of any plan.

In the twinkling of eye he thought and took decision at once. He used the Vakuum brake with full force of his body and breath. He could think this only.

The engine stopped with a big jerk. The jerk affected the compartments, passengers fell down, some bent down to this or that side, but luckily none died.

At least about two thousand passengers were escaped from death. It was a great virtuous deed. But what happened with Daulatram?

The blow of the engine was so fierce that it got Daulatram entangled with the brake badly and he remained in the same position for a long time and Oh! He passed away there entangled with the brake. The flower of humanity fell into dust being faded untimely.

Undoubtedly, Daulatram’s death is the death of martyr. He was one of them who are born but never die and leave their glory forever. Daulatram’s sacrifice is still immortal. That is to illuminate the dark path of humanity.

4. In the dreadful darkness of war the fragrance of humanity—

The event relates to the second world-war.

A Japanese soldier was wounded badly. He was bleeding, slowly and slowly growing weak and his face was fading. The black shadow of death was covering him. It was crystal clear that he was on the verge of death his life was only for a few moments.

The latent humanity of an Indian soldier got suddenly awakened even in the battlefield. He thought, ‘He could be enemy but it matters little! But at the moment while dying, he deserves pity. No question arises hostility at the last moments of death!’

He moved to provide tea to the wounded soldier in a small glass having poured down from his bottle. He put the head of the soldier in his lap with a great affection and touched the lips of the soldier with the cup of tea. He said—‘My friend! You noticed the heroism of a soldier of Budddha’s land on the war front, now taste tea with his affectionate hands.’

But oh! What! What a barbarism! Fierce wound to the heart of humanity!

That wicked Japanese in the return of the sympathy pierced the thigh of the Indian soldier with his dagger the Indian soldier began to bleed.

Now, the both fell down. The Indian soldier was wounded but the wound was not total due to the weakness of the Japanese soldier. .

After a few hours the Japanese wounded soldier was brought to the Indian hospital. The Indian soldier’s wound was also bandaged. When he became well, the same Indian soldier again went to him with a cup of tea and returned only when he made him drink tea lovingly. Now, the japanese soldier was feeling afflicted with the emotion of atonement. He was suffering from self-remorse on his action.

The Japanese soldier said—‘Now, I have come to realise why Buddha was born in your country, India only.

‘Humanity is the sweet smelling flower of life blossoming in the night, that smells sweet with fragrance even in the dread of darkness.

5. He who happened to become extraordinary due to his kindness and courage—

A common employee of Railways was there as a gateman named PannaLal Pathak. His duty was to shut the gate of the main road at the time of the train-arrival. What a work of benevolence is possible in such a work of little importance? You will say, ‘No work of benevolence is possible here.’

But your presumption is not right.

The Barauda-Mathura passenger train was arriving at Ratlam station. The signal was down. Pannalal had gone to a side having closed the gate of the road according to his duty. It was eight in the night. By chance, three women labourers were coming back to their homes having finished their work of the whole day. They were tired and anxious to meet their children. The train was at a little distance. They thought to cross the line hurriedly. They came out through the wire guage silently. By chance their clothes got entangled with the wire guage and they came to a miserable condition.

Anyhow, after overcoming this problem they had hardly reached the rail line when they heard the jolting sound of the train and they got perturbed. They lost their courage. The rail engine was just in front of them to crush them to pieces.

Pannalal saw all this and showing a great courage he jumped upon the line.

In the same breath he pressed both the ladies in his arms and dragged them out of the railway line.

Now the train was just before; it was the next sight of death; yet he did not lose his patience and jumped to save the third female labourer, but alas!

The angry engine gave him a fierce blow and threw him away and the pitiless engine moved ahead crushing the third female labourer.

Panna Lal became unconscious in this struggle and it seemed that he would not be saved then.

But in the hospital he was treated under special care. The doctors tried their best to drag away this foremost chief of humanity from the jaws of death. God always supports the noble deeds. By luck, he recovered his health.

On the table, when he came back to his consciousness, these were the words that came out of his mouth—

‘What happened with the third woman?’ ‘Bravo the man! Even in these moments of death he had no care for his own self but his mind was absorbed in the worry of that third female labourer.’

The latent humanitarian attitude may awaken anytime and do the wonderful act of benevolence. The deeds, which are not done, by any worldly temptation or greed, are done in the divine influence all of a sudden. This sleeping spirit motivates him very fast after awakening his divine spirit towards the virtuous deeds of benevolence.

अद्या नो देव सवित: प्रजावत्् सावी: सौभगम्।

परा दु:ष्वप्न्यं सुव॥

(Rigved 5/82/4)

Mind it— ‘Those, who do the work of benevolence and prowess along with adoration, become free from sorrow and poverty and their prosperity increases.

 

The glimpse of God in men’s inner-self

विद्याविनयसम्पन्ने ब्राह्मणे गवि हस्तिनि।

शुनि चैव श्वपाके च पण्डिता: समदर्शिन:॥

(Gita 5/18)

‘The wise look with equanimity on all whether it be a Brahmana with learning and culture, a cow, an elephant, a dog and a pariah, too.

The kind great soul

The qualities of great man are reflected even in their actions of no importance. The sharp talented persons judge through these qualities that this man is to rise high in future.

Ò Ò Ò Ò

It was morning. It was about 7 a.m. of the day. People were on their morning walk. A youth was also coming walking carefree and in an easy mood absorbed in thoughts.

His attention is just diverted towards the side of the road. What is this? Oh! What an odious sight it is!

There is a dog. Close to his ears there is a wound. Probably, this poor creature is the victim of someone’s hurt with hard wood. It is bleeding. The flies are buzzing. Foul smell is spreading. He is fluttering his ears again and again being afflicted with the pain; The flees fly away for a short while, but again sit overt the wound and begin to defile it and suck the blood.

The youth remained presuming the dog’s pain. Oh! What a pathetic sight! This dog can neither speak, nor get it bandaged and dressed by the doctors. Who is there to realise his pain? The spirituality pricked his mind.

He turned back from his morning walk. Now he was stepping fast towards the medical centre of an Ayurvedic doctor.

‘Vaidyaji! There is the need of a person for the dressing of a patient. The patient’s condition is very serious.’ He said in a pathetic tone. In the hope of the customer, the Vaidya asked anxiously, ‘Speak without any hesitation, who is ill at the residence?’

The youth said—‘There is none ill at my home, one who is patient is not considered by me less than anyone of my family members by any way.’

The Vaidya asked, ‘Who is that one?’

The youth said in a very painful voice, ‘Near the ears of a forlorn dog his wound has been infested with worms. He is restless with pain. He cannot sit even for a moment in comfort. He is fluttering his ears in restlessness again and again. I am very much worried and grieved at his serious condition. Kindly give some medicine without any delay.’

‘Fie! you are worried so much for this only—the Vaidyaji said, ‘For such the trivial dog, you have created such a storm! I had become perturbed to see your facial appearance of perturbance.

He gave a medicine.

Then, laughing he said—‘My dear friend! Keep yourself guarding while doing good. Ultimately an animal is animal only. In the condition of pain the dog becomes about half mad-remains always restless............we apply the medicine hardly on the human patient. It is not an easy task to apply the medicine on a sick and wounded dog.’

The Vaidyaji was speaking on. The resolute youth paid no heed to his words. He came running to the dog. The wounded dog was now more restless. The flies had disturbed him badly by their sting. Many others were also passing by that way. While going on the path they looked towards it with hateful glance and making a face and casting the glance of contempt, moved ahead fast. Without hating the foul smell, the youth, neither pressed his nose nor was he frightened with his bite.

With a courage after wrapping a bamboo stick with cloth he dipped the stick into the medicine and getting the cloth soaked with medicine, touched the would with it mildly. The sharp medicine showed a fast effect on the dog’s wound, the dog got agitated. He tried to bite also but the courageous youth kept on doing the service, he did not bother for it at all. He remained absorbed in his work of benevolence.

The sick dog felt some relief and peace. Due to the effect of the medicine the wound was caused coolness and the flies also flew away by its foul smell. The dog felt comfort.

Now, he was lying peacefully and the youth was using the medicine properly coming closer to him. By waging his tail the dog was expressing his gratitude. He had realized that this man was any god of the previous birth. He had saved him from death.

Whereas the white coloured persons did not pay any attention towards the wounded dog, contrary to it this youth’s heart had melted with pity.

Do you know what was the name of this man? It was Mahamana Pandit Madan Mohan Malviya who had brought a revolutionary change in India in the Hindu religion. Indian culture and in the field of education he had invested the most part of his life in educating the country.

The greatness of great persons starts illuminating from the very beginning.

 

The youth to sacrifice his life for others

America! The busy bank of a river! Awakeness and rare movement! It is early in the morning. The people are coming and going on the side of the river for bath. Some are enjoying the river water sitting on bank of the river being tired of walk and they are watching the rising waves and playfulness of the fishes springing with the waves. There is peace in the atmosphere, there is freshness and joy in the air.

‘Save, O save my child, anyone!’ A heart-touching voice of a woman was heard from a corner. It attracted everyone’s attention. The mother was pointing out towards the river weeping bitterly. Unfortunately her child had fallen down into the river and on the surface of the water was crying ‘Just drowned, just drowned.’

The pathetic cry of the woman had spread all around till now. The people could not control. They gathered running at the spot of accident. Now, it was a good rush there. There was perturbation in everyone.

‘Save, O my son is drowning. Oh! Oh!! He will die, O! Anyone, show courage! save the child from the water!’ The mother was bitterly crying in pathetic lamentation.

Most of the people were simply the spectators standing there; but none dared to jump into the river and save the child. The life was dear to all. Why to die for the son of else one, If one drowns, let him drown!

‘Save, Oh, now just he will drown! Protect! Save!’ Just the moment a youth of about eighteen to nineteen years of age coming through the crowd with the speed like wind reached the river bank and jumped flat taking the aim of the child. All were in the amazement. What happened?

Was he not afraid of the strong current of the river? Had he no attachment with his life? Is he the victim of strong emotions and sentiments or hurriedness? Who knows! The fast flow of the river might swallow him!

Now all are concentrated to watch the youth’s method of swimming. Several times the youth seems to be entangled with the whirpool. Sometimes his mouth and nose seem to be fill with water badly, Several times he escapes hardly to be dashed with the hard hidden rocks. He is really, searching the child by taking dip.

It has taken long time in searching the child. All are looking with anxious eyes searching the youth at the spot of the occurence. He has not come out of the water where has he disappeared?

Isn’t it that he drowned in the water? It appears no hope of his return. Probably he passed away from the world forever.

But after some moments!

His black hair are somewhat visible on the water surface. Mark! Now he is seen swimming on the surface of the water. The moving legs are clearly visible. He is coming towards the river bank.

O God! The fainted child is also in his arms. After a little while the people see that the youth is putting the fainted child before his wailing mother.

He is fainted with fear. He has drunk some water. He will be well soon. Now take care, your child is safe.’ The mother is staring at the youth with the grateful eyes. The child was taken away to the hospital and by luck his life was saved. It was the youth’s courage and effort that brought back the life of the child from jaws of death even. Who was aware of that the child would be saved from the accident? The Lord’s grace is boundless.

Do you know this youth to sacrifice his own life for others?

It was the ex president of very big country like America, George Washington.

ये पायतो मामतेयं ते अग्ने, पश्यन्तो अन्धं दुरितादरक्षन्।

ररक्ष तान्त्सुकृतो विश्वेदा, दिप्सन्त इन्द्रियवो नाह दे भु:॥

Remember—‘A man should never be afraid of contempt, blame, humiliation etc., in the cause of benevolence and goodness. Don’t pay heed to what others remark.

The Lord, Himself, protects such benevolents and the removers of others sorrow and pain. So, being balanced of mind and carefree one should remain always engaged in the public welfare and noble deeds. Here lies the greatness of man.

It is more useful and easy to see the Lord’s sight in the human beings themselves than to search Him in the temples and ‘Mutths’, which are their bases.

 

By the support of labour and prowess a labourer’s son became a learned man

His father was a labourer getting the monthly wages of Rupees two or three. His life was full of financial and social problems. It was hard for him to satisfy the hunger even. It was sufficient if anyhow the cloths were available to wear. The shoes and caps were the objects of luxury for them. If even the food was not available to the stomach’s fill then where was the question of other items like sweet or of a sweetened preparation rice and of milk, boiled together, a cake fried in ghee; chat and Pakauri? These items were the objects of dream for him.

The child began to grow up in the same hardships circumstances of suffocation and poverty gradually. The family was anyhow pulling on. Then, how could that father think of educating his child?

But that labourer father saw the fashionable sons of the rich persons in high quality garments suited-booted with grand looking bags going to school by cycle or car. No doubt he was tempted and wished that his son should also become educated and able, in him the science and knowledge of the world had become worthy of honour in the civilised society.

But curse to the financial helplessness! He had nothing in his pocket to bear the expenses of school charges and buy the books, manage for the school uniform and when his son demands for the pocket expenses like other students what will be answer?

The father always thought all these and kept on the ambitions in his mind.

Now, the child had grown up somewhat matured. When he saw the other boys of the village going to school with their school bags, he used to catch the corner of his father’s clothes and with tears in his eyes said—

‘Father! All the boys of the village go to school to study with slate and pencils. I will also go. Bring books and slate for me also. I will also become great after getting education. I will also work as a clerk by sitting in the chair. It is the education that makes anyone great and famous. I will study with the concentrated mind and become a learned one.

The father stared the child with tearful eyes. He caressed his hands on the head of the son affectionately. Then, wiping his tears with great affection, describing his condition of poverty and helplessness before him he used to say—

‘Son! You have intense inclination for education you crave for getting knowledge from books. These are the symptoms of greatness. Your old impressions are very high and Sattvika. What a nice had it been if you would have been born in a rich family? Oh! Why were you born in this poor family? If your destiny had favoured you to become great, you would have not been the son of a poor like me. Oh! Curse to my poverty! I am unable to manage a little to educate my dearest son!’

While saying so tears streamed forth from his father’s eyes. His heart used to throb fast. He used to cling his dear son to his bosom with great affection and the sense of mineness. When he returned to normalcy from the upsurge of the emotion he said—

‘Son! Don’t be disappointed. If winter comes can spring be far behind! Being grown up more, think of doing some labour so that first we may fill our stomach. And then in the spare time you may study also. I have no money at all in my pocket. At present to think of the study is quite useless.

Having heard the father’s talk of financial affairs, the boy had to suppress his feelings. What in fact this innocent child of small age but could do?

But his intense secret craving to become learned after being educated remained deep-rooted in his mind and day by day it surged up.

Even in the adverse miserable condition and poverty and despite discouraging reply of his father his courageous and zealous sentiment did not minimise. He was in search of favourable opportuning. Along with perseverance he had sufficient modesty and civility. He was sweet in tongue with everyone. His modest behaviour made many his friends. He befriended such good and gentle students who allowed him to read their books in spare time. Not only to this limit, but they who came being well educated after paying costly fees in the shools, used to teach this poor boy also something.

When the other rich boys played, this boy used to study in the streets in the dim light of the street lamps of the municipality.

He had no slate and pencils. He used to practise writing on the ground with the burnt coal. Someone gave him a pencil showing mercy. Then, he began to learn the alphabets by writing on the papers thrown as useless papers on the roads and streets. He learnt many words and sentences orally. Many lessons and stories of the syllabus books were committed to his memory.

The father began to curse for his poverty to see his perseverence. His heart also became restless to see his son’s hard labour and sharp wit and to make him educated.

This was the first chapter of the child’s life.

The life took the second turn. The new page of his life started. His poor father made a plan for more earning.

One day, with the purpose of more earning he set out towards Calcutta near his village with his son. He had no fare of the train. He started his journey on foot.

On the way he halted to take rest. The tired father said—‘I don’t know how long have I come?’

Unexpectedly the boy answered, ‘Nine miles father.’

The father was astonished.

‘How did this boy come to know it?’ he was thinking in his mind.

The boy himself explained—‘Father! It is written ‘nine’ on the close mile-stone.

The explaination of the answer was the sign of the child’s sharp wit. The father was overwhelmed with joy to see it.

The child Ishwar Chandra learnt the English numbers while going with his father. Due to the sharp talent of his son, again he fell into contemplation and returned with him.

On the way, he remained thinking—‘It will be a great crime towards such an inquisitive child to deprive him of the study due to poverty. I resolve that I will take my food only once a day keep all the family members to depend on only one meal but I will send Ishwar Chandra to school at any cost.

This resolve became the base of the child’s progress.

Coming back home he got Ishwar Chandra admitted in the school of his village. The boy studied with devotion and concentration of mind. He acquired the highest knowledge of his course book. He proved to be the best student of his school. All the teachers admired him excessively. Now, he had completed the study in that school.

It was impossible for a poor father to continue his study further away from the village. So, he had to refuse to continue his education; because it was beyond his capacity to bear the expences of his education further onward.

Then, Ishwar Chandra requested to get him admitted in any school, He will meet the expences of fees and education anyhow by doing the work of labour—He, himself, will search any job in the city.

The father agreed and got him admitted in a Sanskrit school of Calcutta. On account of his devotion, service and perseverence, Ishwar Chandra pleased the teachers of the college so much that he was exempted from the fees. He had become the sharer of his friends for the books.

By this way, he went on increasing his qualifications gradually. Constantly he went on rising up. Till the age of nineteen, he was well versed in Sanskrit Grammar, Literature, Figures of speech, Vedanta, Shastras. He became a great learned man of the country. Being impressed by his unequivocal knowledge and dignified conduct, an assembly of scholars honoured him with the title ‘Vidyasagar’ along with a certificate of honour and in his valuation he was offered the post of professorship in Sanskrit with due respect and request in the Fort William College of Sanskrit.

By the virtue of labour and intelligence a labourer’s son became the historical man of India. His name was Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar.

 

The glimpses of God in human being

पुरुष एवेदॸसर्वम्।

(Rigved 10/90/2)

Means—‘This entire universe is the form of the Supreme Lord. Considering the world as the manifestation of God, it should be served.’

The God is always present in the human mind and numberless times He illumines in the form of divine traits. The God has done extraordinary labour in the creation of human beings, its fruitfulness is only when man remains engaged in the fulfilment of divine purposes and benevolence for which he has been created. To make this world pleasant and well managed, The formless Supreme Lord needed a form, which had its consummation in the form of human being.

From time to time such examples are seen in our society and daily life which prove the existence of God in our inner self and He prompts us to do noble deeds. Such examples are quoted here.

Life-donation to save the patient

A surgeon Dr. Sudhir Gopal Jhingaran of N.E.R. Central hospital Gorakhpur in the Eastern U.P. sacrificed his life to save the life of a patient. It is so, the patient had been operated. The patient was weak already from the beginning and he had the shortage of blood in his body. His blood was tested and classified in group. After testing the blood of many persons the blood of his group could not be available. By chance, the surgeon Dr. Sudhir Gopal tested his own blood and it was of the same blood group of the patient. The blood of only the doctor could save the patient and there was not other way to save the patient. Now what to do?

Doctor Saheb began to think, ‘To raise ourselves higher above the materialistic narrowness, we will have to think that we have been blessed with this human class of birth for the welfare of others for the spiritual thoughts, for the benevolence, service and to accomplish the high ideals. If we do nothing for the human welfare then our human life is worthless. We must do something in the interest of this world—the Cosmic form of manifested God in addition to our body and family sustenance.’

Having thought so, Dr. Sudhir Gopal became ready to donate his blood to the patient. After one bottle of blood the patient came to require one bottle more blood. The doctor was again donating his blood that in the meanwhile some such reactions happened in his body that he died the same night despite the best possible treatment. God’s labour proved fruitful. That divine light extinguished but gave away the lesson to hundreds of souls the duty of human birth.

The Eye-donation of an old woman

In Allahabad the eyes of 70 years old Bengali woman have been jolted to two blinds successfully. The old woman had bequeathed her eyes to the hospital as a donation. She had got written in her will—‘If any part of my body may be used in the welfare of any other one, I consider my life worthful. This is the motive behind the boundless talent, divine knowledge, this human spirit that has been blessed by the God to the mankind that he should remain dedicated in benevolence till the last breath. Let my eyes be kept protected and use them to any needy youth either male or female and God’s creation of mine may prove useful.’

The doctor of the hospital has transplanted her one eye in a ten years old blind girl and the second in 22 years old youth. Both of them have regained the eye-sight.

In the same line there is an other example A six years old girl named Jyotsana Ben Patel of Bombay city donated her eyes after death. This girl had died in the hospital of the city in 1965. The parents of the girl donated her eyes to the Gvt. eye bank at once. As a result the pupils of a blind boy were transformed and one another man was surgically operated for the vitium transplantation.

The news report of Nagpur is as such—In the local Medical College, the donated eyes by a 60 years old woman were transplanted in the eyes of 30 years old young lady. She had lost her eye-sight at the age of five due to the smallpox.

The imitable ideal in the life of scarcity

Even in the afflicted with scarcity and hardships, burdened with the load of many responsibilities there is the glimpse of God.

The matchless ideal presented by the teachers and employees of D.A.V. college, Muzaffarnagar, in the help of teacher’s orphan family on his sudden death is imitable certainly.

Shri Sitaramji, head of the department of economics in the college died on 17th of july 1965. There was left no support for the widow, two sons and four daughters of Shri Sitaramji. The two sons were dependent. They could earn nothing. The earning man became the victim of death. The two daughter should be married without delay.

It is not very difficult to presume the result of the lecturer’s death in such a financial stringency and manage problems and what problems and hurdles would have been created before Shri Sitaramji’s widow? It is not hidden to anyone about the poor financial stringency of the teachers. Their earning remains confined to their livlihood only. There are rare who leave some money after their death. As regards they who have a big family, they have no end of their miseries.

The Lord flashed through the college employees. There was a murmuring in their innerself—‘You should support the family of your late colleague by all means.’ All decided to support the family in misery.

Do you know what was this decision?

All of them including the peons and even the sweepers decided to donate the amount of their D.A. and they would be depositing it for the coming three years. Thus, with the money collected the family will be supported for all the purposes like marriage etc.

It is not difficult to imagine the problems of the teachers and employees who took this vow; but the humanity considers them the ideal who try to solve other problems at the risk of their own sufferings and they are the inspiring ones.

The honesty of a Rikshaw-puller

The news report of Faridkot. The twenty-one years old Rikshaw-puller, Ram Chandra spent his whole day in search of the stranger traveller, who had left his suitcase on the rikshaw by mistake and in hurry he had gone away at his work. That suitcase contained the jewellery worth of about forty-five thousand rupees. If he desire, he could grab the entire wealth, but that Rikshaw-puller understood the moral responsibility of human life and considered his success in fulfilling it. At last, openning the suitcase, with the support of the address written in a letter, he found out the owner of the jewellery and approaching him, he handed over the suitcase as it is. The owner of the jewellery wanted to give the Rikshaw-puller Rupees five hundred as reward. First he refused to accept it. After insistence, he took that money and donated it in the account of ‘Jawaharlal Nehru-Smarak.’

The God in man guides him to the right path. If there is intensity of desire and there is need, firmness and strong assiduity, the path of benevolence is certain.

The atonement of mistake

A news concerning an event of Cuttack has been published in the newspapers. A unique type of occurence of atonement by a student for his mistake has happened. The event is as follow—

A student of class VIIIth of Shekh Bazar came from the city to the station by Rikshaw. He gave a note of Rupee one to the Rikshaw-puller to pay twelve annas as Rikshaw fare, but the Rikshaw-puller returned the note because he had no change of four annas to return. The student having said, ‘Just I bring the change. Stay for awhile—went on the platform inside and he was absorbed in reading the magazine on the book stall so much that he forgot that he had to give the fare even to the Rikshaw-puller.

After half an hour when he came to remember taking the change from the book stall he rushed out of the station but unfortunately he could not find the Rikshaw-puller there. The innerself of the student disturbed him badly. He began to think—‘Oh! What a sin I committed! I grabbed the wage of a poor labourer! I deprived a poor man of his food. He would be hungry being in a sad mood. While searching for, it became late he began weeping in sobs in the night; yet he could not be found out. Just near the motor stand. When the people enquired of the cause of his weeping, he explained to them as it was and began to say—‘A poor Rikshaw-puller was deprived of his wages due to my mistake. I am compunctioning for it.’

After the persuation by others, he went home by another Rikshaw with tears in his eyes but he donated twelve annas to the other crippled beggars before he departed.

It is true that if the internal ambition is firy, to fulfil it if there is firm resolve and strong effort, the way of benevolence occurs to one’s mind. Anyway becomes veritable to offer support or service to others.

Sacrifice for benevolence

A man naming Anand Rao belonging to Chhindwara district Jabalpur has been honoured with the president award after death of sacrificing his life to save the life of a child who was drowning. As it is said that a ten years old child was playing on the weak cover of steel covering a deep pit of drains. That covering could not bear the load of the child and suddenly collapsed. It was filled with water upto a good height. Late Sri Anand Rao was standing near by. He did not care for his own life to save the child’s life and he, himself jumped into the pit. Though, he was successful in his purpose, but he died due to the poisonous gas and air of the pit due to choking of breath before he could come out. For this great heroic deed of benevolence, the government of India appreciated it and has awarded him ‘The President Award’.

In the same line an other news—

New Delhi. By saving the life of three ladies from drowning at the risk of his own 16 years old boy naming Subhas Chandra’s father, R.R. Khurana was awarded with ‘Life-Saving-Award’ (First class) posthumously by the chief commissioner in a meeting organised at his residence.

The whole event is as such—Subhas Chand the student of Kamarshal Higher Secondary School of Dariaganj was wandering about with his three friends near Kudasiaghat on 8th of November 1962 when a loud cry was heard from the Ghat side. They at once reached the ghat running. They came to know that a few women had been caught into a whirlpool. Having put off his shoes, Subhas jumped into the river, Yamuna in his dress on his body. He saved all the three drowning women but could not save himself and sank into the Yamuna river. When the story of this benevolent boy was narrated in the organised meeting, his father’s forehead raised high with pride.

There is hidden divinity inside the mankind and its glimpse reflects from time to time. By benevolence man’s divinity develops more and more. By adopting this attitude a man becomes god, gets peace and becomes famous and gets joy in this world and the next world.

The Post Office without employee

In a village of Rajkot (Saurashtra) a post office without any employee is running successfully just to make an experiment. In that village of Junagarh the postcards and envelops have been kept in a box. Anyone who needs takes out and drops the money of its cost. Due to this honesty that Post office is running properly. This Post office has not suffered from the loss of even a single rupee till now. By developing the tendency of doing good, man proceeds towards divinity and presents the atmosphere like heaven.

I can do nothing against rules

Saint Socrates was sentenced to death. The people had not understood his ideology rightly. There are enough foolish-minded in the world. Due to this reason, Socrates was in condemned cell of the jail as a prisoner who has been sentenced to death.

His most favourite pupil, Crito thought of a plan to save him. He wanted to save him by anyway right or wrong. By giving bribe, Crito entered the jail secretly and spoke before Socrates with folded hands—

‘I have managed in all respects to save your life. Don’t delay and escape from the jail silently. All the arrangements outside the jail to run away safely, have already been made. Nobody will get any clue of your escape from the jail. You will be made to reach any other country. The entire earning of my whole life is presented to your feet. Well! Only your life is required.’

It was a golden opportunity for Socrates to protect his life. Who is there such a man whose life is not dear to him? A man wants to protect his life by anyway, proper or improper.

But on his proposal Socrates answered soberly— ‘I cannot accept such immoral proposal. I consider it a deceit to the God by going against the rules of that country where I was born, where my mother and father have been living, where I have breathed in the air and where I have been brought up.’

In reality, the base of spiritual exaltation is not any method of worship, rituals or the practice of spirituality but the living of the divine qualities, honesty and will to stick to the discipline can be the base only. For the attainment of God, heaven, salvation and spiritual peace, the essential factors are self-control, moral conduct and magnanimity without their achievement how can be worthy of redemption?

Corpse Donation of Ownself

Sr. Ed. V. Narsingh Rao an advocate of Gudar in Hyderabad has already donated till now; his blood forty times to save the life of the patients but his tradition of sacrifice and renunciation has yet not stopped. He considers the service of God in the service of the humanity. He wants to make the human life fruitful. So, he has bequeathed his dead body to the Osmania General Hospital—Superintendent’s name in his will. He has said this also in his will that his eyes should be kept reserve for the needy.

Old Widow’s all in all given in charity

An old lady named Smt. Joharia Bai has donated her entire property in charity to the State government to open a girls School in her village Siwani in the district Bilaspur.

The widow donated her property to the Dy. Finance minister of Madhya Pradesh, Sri S.P. Dubey at the time when he was delivering a speech in a public meeting in the village. When the local leader was greeting the minister, the old woman went up on the dais and handed over the papers of her land costing seven hundred rupees and one thousand five hundred in cash to him. She gave words to donate rupees five hundred more in the near future. This old woman appealed to the Dy. minister to start the construction work of the school soon so that she might see the school flourishing in her life time. She says that the devotion of God is inherent in the expansion and discrimination of knowledge. To provide opportunity to others to acquire knowledge is the real worship.

The dutifulness of a peon

The robbers thrashed badly to a school peon named Shri Durgaprasad of Bulandshahar and looted his all the cash. When they began to snatch his cycle forcibly, he resisted stubbornly. That cycle was the school property and thus, it was his moral and pious duty to protect the public property. He did not give this cycle to them until they fired shots and made him fall down on the ground. That peon was the employee of Sharma Higher Secondary School, Bulandsahar.

He was going to his village to attend an important work when on the way the robbers surrounded him. They took all the cash what he had with him forcibly. When they began to take away his cycle forcibly, he said in the humble words—‘You can take all my possessions but I cannot give you the belonging of the school at any cost; because this is a public property. I consider it most important to guard it.’

The dutifulness is the great worship of the God. There is the source of constant overflow of virtues and noble deeds in benevolent human heart; because God remains present in his mind in the inanimate form.

प्रजापति:....बहुधा वि जायते।

(Atharvaved 10/8/13)

Means—‘In this world it is the God who is taking birth in different forms. All the living beings of the world are the manifistations of God.’

Mind it—

मर्त्या हवाअग्ने देवा आसु:।

(Shat. Brahman. 11/1/2/12)

Means—‘The human beings in this world become god by noble and virtuous deeds. Do the good deeds however you may do and attain the position of god of earth by this body. They who fulfil the moral duty, are gods.’

 

Sacrifice and love

The excellent fruit of virtuous deed is inevitable

There is the hidden moral rule of law of the Supreme God guiding the whole universe. There is the abundance of spirituality present inside the human beings and it leads him towards noble deeds. The man leading his life according to this moral divine rule of law remains always happy, healthy and talented and fully contented. Contrary to it, the man following the immoral polluted path of sin, remains suffering from distress; disturbance and self-contempt in his inner life.

In the words of Prof. Laljiram Shukla—‘Man behaves against the moral law in passion and demonical frenzy, guided by selfish motive or due to ignorance but he has to bear the punishment of the God for his immoral conduct. After suffering from pain he comes to the right path of nobility. For the noble and auspicious deeds pleasure, contentment and self-satisfaction and for the sin, disease, sorrow, dissatisfaction is the real fact. This rule is fully in accordance with reason.

The lives of numberless persons have revealed this truth. The moral conduct has provided them wonderful benefit. Here, some experiences of such persons are being quoted in their own words—

Virtuous deed saved from the hanging

Sri Gopal Newatia has written his experiences in connection with Ram Lal Nai (the barber) in the following words—

‘That day, while massaging his body Ram Lal Nai asked him, ‘Babuji, Was the case of Bombay decided?

I startled a bit! What astonishing one side Bombay and the otherside this rural village! Before I could reply he again said—

‘You will see, Babuji he will be acquitted by the jury; but I have marked the eyes of the judge. He will not acquit him.

The words of the Nai confined to the Nai! What this judge, how his eyes and this Ram Lal the witness! But it did not stop here, it continued—

‘Babuji! The Bombayite fired shots only, but I had used the dagger, in twice three pieces............!’

Hardly I heard than I jumped and sat down.

He said, ‘Babuji! Don’t get startled up. Ram Lal is not now a murderer but the servant of your majesty! Yes! But the hands are the same that had used the sword.’

It came to my mind to ask when, whom and why he killed? But I did not consider it proper to interrupt his narration to be deprived of the taste. Ram Lal continued his story—

‘In my case, thousands of my villagers gathered in the courtyard of the court and made prayer of my acquital. But, my lord! The day I stepped in the court and my eyes looked on the face of the judge, I came to understand that the fact was not hidden to him. And it happened so also as I have already been sentenced for being hanged to death.’

My amazement had no bound to hear this because Ram Lal the convict of hanging-sentence was physically present before my very eyes presuming my curiocity, he began to say himself—

‘Babuji! There is nothing astonishing here. This is all the fruit of the past noble deeds. The act of benevolence is the true religion. The God repays a good return of our every noble and meritorious act. If we do any noble work even hidden, the virtuous deed remains deposited like money deposited in the bank and does the work of armour in the difficult days. The God repays the return of our every work either good or bad.

राम झरोखे बैठिके, सबको मुजरा लेय।

जाकी जैसी चाकरी, वाको वैसो देय॥

This Ram is the second name of moral rule. Since I had come to senses, I had an attitude of benevolence and doing service and help of others in the best possible way. In any fair or gathering in the neighbourhood all the time for day and night I used to make the thirsty persons drink the water. I have distributed grams among the hungry persons from my own pocket, I have donated cloths to the beggars, I have provided medical treatment to the animals; I have never cut any green tree, I have never done any immoral deed, this is the collected fruit of all the noble deeds, that this Ram Lal escaped from being hanged.’

I was taking interest in the occurence of Ram Lal’s life.

He was not only acquitted from death sentence but from the punishment of 25 years in the jail also. It was all the reward of his noble deeds and ............ and .......... Babuji! if you want I should tell its secret also.

I was already taking interest in these expereinces just like in detective stories. So I nodded head in agreement. Being stimulated Ram Lal again began to narrate.

‘Now, just you see, how much does the merits remain collected and helps the man in his rainy days? Hearing the news of death-sentence, my wife wept bitterly but I had not any trace of agony on my face. I was confident that the devotee of the Lord, who had fallen by chance into trouble, could not die premature death, then where is the question of death sentence? I have seen the convicts of death-sentence in the jail, their condition becomes worse than that of hell till the decision of appeal. To live, to eat, to sleep, toilet all in a single room and the worst is as if a naked sword is hanging on the head. But believe my lord! Ram Lal had full faith in the God’s moral justice. That he would not be hanged and it so happened also. I appealed in the higher court and there the punishment was minimised to twenty five years of imprisonment only. The God granted me my life.

‘Twenty-five years! This punishment was also exempted.’

‘No, my lord! There also my previous noble deeds rescued me. This was the secret reward of leading my life according to the moral rules of conduct that I got. Just after two years a war broke out and it was announced that the prisoners who would like to go to fight in the war would be exempted from punishment. Well! What more needed? Hundreds of prisoners like me became ready and it took the form of an army. Whereon one side this long imprisonment, shackles, handmill and other troubles and the other side this army-uniform, food, open air and carefree life. This was all the result of merits. It is only the moral law of the Supreme that protects under such circumstances.

I saw a number of countries as a soldier of the army. Even went and came from America but mark this hidden support of God! I simply a prisoner of jail was travelling throughout the world.’

I asked—‘Ram Lal! Did you fight ever?’

He said—‘Babuji! Enough! It was the only desire that remained unfulfilled. In the war the use of dagger is far away, even the opportunity to touch the butt to any one’s body could not be available! That was the war of hand-grenade and bomb. The chance to fire with gun was also only once, at the time of roll-call when the bullet from any side came and pierced into the thigh.’

While describing this Ram Lal’s chest puffed up. I cast my praising look. He went on narrating—

‘The bullet hurt me but I was conscious. In usual way after being wounded, the death comes before eyes but I tell you truly Babuji! I was confident that the Lord was finding out some way to save me from this trouble also. Then, such was divine device really. I felt as if who had released me from noose of hanging and relieved me from the twenty five years of imprisonment, this amassed capital of virtuous deeds will support me this time also and Babuji! You see it is the support of that Almighty that has made me to sit in this position before you remaining alive.’

It was beyond my imagination that the life of a village barber could be so full of events; but the influence of noble deeds was quite true. Ram Lal had been discharged from the army also on the ground of sickness.

With this experience it is clear that the acts of noble deeds are the source of lifelong benefits. The acts done according to the moral wisdom provide spiritual force.

One whose innerself is illuminated with spiritual knowledge, becomes capable to know one’s vices and the sentiment is created to remove them as soon as possible. Where there is light, there is no possibility of darkness. In the same way where there is moral wisdom, the hidden support will be there without the least doubt. The devotion to God means the feeling of love, benevolence service to all the living beings. The only way to love the God enshrining all beings and do the moral duty is to relieving them of their sufferings and to make them happy as far as we can do earnestly. Righteousness is not to be confined to the tongue only but it is to be given practical stablity through actions.

Dady, used to sit there to guide the right way to the travellers

Miss Sunanda (Bombay) has written an event occured in Western countries as follows—

That year, I was on a visit of ‘Switzerland’ in summer. The direct road going to ‘Gathard mountain pass’ was passing near my rented house to stay there in Lugano; but another road also was going somewhere else from there—On the hill usually, the travellers might have been catching that road by mistake. But just beside my house, there lived an old gentleman.

In the house there were only two members—he and his daughter Leena. In any accident the gentleman had lost his energy to walk. So he had to take the support of wheelchair to move anywhere. He was a great benevolent and given to service. He considered it piety to use his body in ‘others’ service whatever could be possible by him. Because of his feeling of service he got up early in the morning daily and pushing his chair anyhow he reached there where the road had been divided into two directions. He used to sit there till the sun-set reading books under the shade of a tree. Leena brought tea, breakfast etc., for him there.

When my curiosity grew intense, one day I asked Leena—‘Why does the old dady sit on the side of the road instead of taking rest?”

Hearing my question she remained silent for a moment. Then said—‘My dady has the dominant humanitarian feeling of service to the mankind as a whole. His legs are meaningless even then he wants to serve the travellers more and more. All the beings of the world fulfil the desire of their welfare, pleasure and self-interest themselves but dady is of the view that man is blessed with the abundance of opportunities to become more thoughtful, considerate and wise and its true usefulness lies in dedicating himself in the welfare of the world. He should be guided by the feeling of human welfare. Dady sits there to guide the right path to the travellers. If any traveller turns to the wrong direction he guides him the right direction.’

It is his version—‘If I could make my worthless life worthful for others even by this way, I would be feeling pleasure of life. What we say, let it be practised in our own life first, it will give a good reaction itself. By fondling even the beasts and birds begin to show affinity then what to talk of mankind? He remains always fond of affinity. You do good to others and your good is served first. Every particle spent for the welfare of others comes back numberless times more. My soul feels a great joy, peace and contentment by this work of guidance.’

From Michigan, Sweden, Brazil etc., he has got letters of gratitude also for guiding the travellers. Dady considers these letters the invaluable treasure.

While saying this, Leena’s throat choked and I was amazed to see the feelings of social service of that man guiding the travellers sitting under the tree.

This memoir makes it clear that if a man lives a truthful life, it is good enough. The true glory of man is in the fact that should be called a man of virtue, civilized, cultured and gentle. The man’s ambition should be to be possessed of the rich store of humane virtues in excess. The best criterion of anyone’s progress, prosperity and intelligence is that he should enhance his divine humanitarian virtues overcoming his vices and make his life ideal and exemplary. Among the human duties the greatest objective is the self-evolution. There can be nothing more success in life than the service of the mankind.

The unique feeling of benevolence of a criminal

This is a news of Bermingham. A criminal whose name was William Boven had committed the murder of his wife in 1961. After five years of the case trial, he was convicted for the murder and awarded the punishment of death-sentence. Before death sentence, the criminal was asked for his last wish. He said—‘I am unlucky that I could do no virtuous deed in my lifetime but before death my moral wisdom has awakened and I want to do any work of benevolence so that I may die peacefully. Before death I want to do such a work as may be set an example for future and may prove to be the source of inspiration for the other unfortunates like me. I have decided that my both the eyes should be donated to any blind to provide them sight. I am sorry that any other part of my body cannot be useful for anyone otherwise I would have given them also.’

According to the last wish of the criminal his both the eyes were taken out and seating him on the chair of electricity he was sentenced to death. The eye-surgeon planted his one eye to a blind old man and the second eye to a blind young girl and thus, they began to see.

A virtuous Rikshaw-puller

A news of Roorky is as such—A teacher’s mother fell ill seriously. He called in a doctor for treatment in hurry. But unfortunately the teacher’s old mother had died before the doctor came. The teacher asked the doctor to excuse and said—‘Sorry for your trouble you have taken to come here.’

The doctor answered—‘No matter. Well! Please pay Rupees five as the fees of my visit.’ Fees without treatment! Begging pity and with helpless glance the teacher saw towards the doctor. The pathetic wailing cry of his wife and children was being heard coming from inside the house. But the doctor left the place when he got his fees. He was not the least pitiful.

The teacher had brought the doctor by a Rikshaw. He gave eight annas to the Rikshaw-puller as its fare; but he refused to accept this money. While departing, he spoke in a sweet voice—

‘As your mother has died and I should charge the fare? I am not the doctor, but a poor Rikshaw-puller. It is the man who supports at the time of misery. My heart is not a stony heart.’

The teacher said to him—‘You have done labour. You have shed your sweat; that is why you are entitled of wages.’ Please, accept it.’

But the Rikshaw-puller went away without taking the fare.

The doctor of materialistic view and the Rikshaw- puller of the spiritual view are the examples for us to follow. Really, the religion means to assist in maintaining the society well arranged, well controlled and well developed. But it is a matter of sorrow that such religion should be given importance. That importance is not being given today but unless that feeling to serve others likewise does not develop. The feeling of serving of a man as one ownself is present unless in every particle develops in the human beings even the strict rule of law cannot check up the vices of mankind. We should feel proud of following the divine moral rules and having faith in them. Let us go on developing virtues in us.

By developing the divine merits in our conduct and behaviour only our society can progress. Out of the religious treaties ordained in the ‘Smritis, Sacrifice, forgiveness, kindness, equanimity, service and benevolence are the foremost. If these divine properties are to provide peace and contentment in the individual life, that can be conducted in the society also. As a result its fruitfulness in social life is also but natural.

The auspicious deed depends on the purity of innersense. The more purity is in our mind and reason the more auspicious work will be done by us. He who becomes noble by nature cannot do evil deeds even if he befalls in adverse situations.

Generally, a common man thinks that he will be exempted from the fruit of his evil deeds by worship, muttering, austerity, Yagya, fast, the sight of gods etc. But it is certain that we have to bear the fruit of virtues and sin at any cost. It is an other thing that some times virtues dominate the vices and sometimes the vices dominate the virtues. If the merits increase the sins minimise. If the evils increase, the sins go on increasing.

Man is the store of both—the virtues and vices. By the study of Mahabharat we come to know that whereas Duryodhan, Karn etc., had the demerits, they had praiseworthy merits also. Due to the excess of evils the Kauravas were defeated and due to the excess of merits the Pandavas were winners.

The highest merit is to go to the shelter of the preceptor (Gurudev), God or Supreme Lord and obey their bidding. The Lord exempts him from all the evils who has got this merit.

 

Self-effort is the best

You consider that you can progress in your life only by the support of others. We depend on others. We require their help and support. But as a fact, this thought is wrong point blank.

God has made man complete in himself. Those elements, that cause progress and uplift in life, have been permeated in abundance in him. Man’s mind and spirit is filled with plenty of wonderful mental, moral and spiritual powers. In his evolutionary thoughts there is plenty of material of life formation.

There are different directions of there powers. You are free to follow the path what you want or where to go. Courage and valour, patience and struggle, labour and effort, devotion and knowledge etc., are the different directions of thought. The man who proceeds to anyone of the directions, goes on proceeding a head higher and higher to the same direction by the power of his thought. He takes its advantage by its use in the active field of life.

Our ignorance

Sometimes man remains ignorant of his power for a long time. In want of this true knowledge, he remains floating about aimlessly like the leaf floating in the air. Then, abruptly by the contact or an association with anybody or by fellowship with saints his faith develop in his powers and in the ripe age of his life he starts his progress.

They who are not mindful of their energy hidden in their mind, body and soul, remain poor, agonised and weak throughout their life. In their whole life they fail to attract the attention of the people. Numberless persons of such type were born in this world and like the animals and birds they wasted their life and perished it to the dust. They are the braves and vigorous who deserve the entire enjoyments of this earth. There is nothing in this world for the cowards and idles.

We are amazed at the success of great scientists. We stare in amazement and are astonished on the inventions, invented by them. We stand amazed to see the sky-kissing buildings of the men of riches. We clap with joy to see the demonstration of the artists art and skills. We remain pondering over for a long time on the miracles of the mountaineers riding higher on the peaks of the great mountains. The Western countries have left the fish and birds far behind in the field of ships and aeroplanes. Man is reaching the moon today. These are the wonderful miracles of man’s prowess.

Today, our country is overpowered by cowardiceness and laziness. Such a long period of our independence has passed, but we could not make that progress what was ought to be achieved by us basically. We have failed to remove the illiteracy, non-understanding and poverty of our country. We have failed to increase that production in our fields which was ought to be done. We have not made progress in the field of science and knowledge. It clearly means that we are not hard-working and painstaking to a great extent.

In the Vedas there a very useful saying—

कृतं मे दक्षिणे हस्ते, जयो मे सव्य आहित:।

गोजिद् भूयासमश्वजिद् धनंजयो हिरण्यजित्॥

(Rigved 7/50/8)

It means—‘O the man! Make effort with your right hand and be confident that the success is sure in the left hand, achieve the cows, horses and gold etc., invaluable objects with your hard-working and painstaking efforts.’

This is our great weakness, We repent that we could do nothing in our life. In any sphere of life we could not make any remarkable progress. We are frustrated with failure. Its, reason is clear that we did not make hardworking efforts as the part of our life. Our life and our country could not make that satisfactory progress really which was ought to be done by us on account of laziness and remaining lethargic.

In the moments of helplessness and disappointment, the hidden prowess of our mind proves to be the true supporter for us. When the man stands on his own legs and does not expect any support from others, he comes to stand at the gate of success.

You should be valorous. Take the work and plannings in our own hand with new zeal and courage. Identify yourself of your courage in the sphere of your work what you have taken in hands. Then, it is certain that you are not a coward and weakling.

Mind it that you are endownd with hundreds of types of powers. You have plenty of materials to change the directions of life and society towards the progress. You, yourself, create in you the powers of courage, vigour, efforts, labour, patience and sturggle by your firm resolve and by their use you take advantage in the active sphere of life. If you neglect and don’t become serious about your these divine powers, you will remain miserable and weak throught your life. The braves only deserve the enjoyments of the earth. There is everything in the world—wealth, property, respect, dignity and high status but to gain it, men’s perseverance is needed.
