Bali was wicked, he had lost his consideration of right and wrong and the subject had trembled by his sensuous tortures. There was none to face him in war and kill him. One who came to fight with Bali face to face, his half of the vigour was transfered to Bali automatically. So, Shri Ramchandraji had killed from the back of the tree instead of coming face to face. In the interest of the nation it was justified although it was the act of breaking the general rule of war. The wicked was ultimately punished, whatever the way was adopted.

Similarily in the war between Kauravas and Pandavas, the family preceptor Dronacharya caused a great havoc on the army of the Pandavas and there was a great ruin of their army. The Pandavas got afraid to see it. If the Kauravas had won, it would have been created the reign of injustice and torture. So, Shri Krishna got an elephant named Ashwathama killed. The name of Dronacharya’s son was also Ashwathama. When Dronacharya heard from the mouth of Shri Krishna that Ashwathama was killed, he got perturbed. On this very moment, he was killed. If Drona had not been killed on some pretext, the Kauravas would have won and it would have been the victory of immorality.

In Bihar, a big tyrannical king, named Jarasandh ruled there. He had grabbed about eighty small states of the kings and had kept many queens in his gynaecium of the palace having kidnapped them. The wicked Jarasandh was extremely mighty and no one was capable to face him. That is why Shri Krishna, himself in the disguise of a Brahman accompanied Arjun and Bhim and reached the gynaecium of Jarasandh. There He disclosed Himself a Brahman and in his own palace having managed shrewdly the wrestling between Bhim and Jarasandh, got him killed. In the same way, when Karn killed Arjun’s son by deceit, Shri Krishna took its revenge also.

Thus, from time to time for the repression of torture and wickedness of the world and protection of truth, love, justice, there is a rule of punishment in Indian culture. To punish the wicked by trick, diplomacy or even by hiding ownself with purpose of righteousness or the good of the nation is not immoral. A number of wickeds and demons were subdued and punished and as a result of the same our culture is surviving. ‘शठे शाठ्यं समाचरेत्’ The policy of ‘Tit for tat’, only due to following this policy, our culture is on the top of glory.

Mercy, forgiveness and punishment—judicious use of all these three should be made in human life. Its practice needs cautiousness and intelligence. It is the morality and righteousness to forgive them showing mercy who are weak, helpless, distressed, deserve your support. As divine laws and mercy of God are equal for all, similarily your kindness and forgiveness should be for the whole mankind—It is possible that they may adopt the new path of life by your forgiveness and may start to pass the life of high ideals. If there is such a man of any country, any city, any village or in any condition and if you meet him, who may be uplifted by your kindness, forgive him for his past faults. The feeling of forgiveness, itself, is to create peace and balance to your own heart, it is a joyous elegant instinct to enhance the spiritual happiness and joy. He who wants undecaying pleasure, should remain free from the feeling of jealousy, malice and hostility. Forgiveness and kindness will free you from these wicked sentiments.

Practice the use of punishment after well consideration. Attention! On the basis of individual hostility to do injustice is such a type of two-edged dagger which wounds the weak but it does not spare even the strong.

 

Man becomes god by self-restraint

According to Indian culture man’s view point should be high. In our culture soul has been given priority. The Hindu fundamentalists have thought over the way of life, worldly behaviour, objects and individual method of living life and the fundamental principles with the spiritual point of view. Going above trivial worldly enjoyments of pleasure and comforts, having developed spiritual feeling the priority has been given to live the life of spirituality. Keeping in view the protection of morality the recognitions have been prescribed here in our culture.

The Indian sages had made researach that man’s endless ambition, the achievement of happiness and peace, cannot be possible with the worldly or materialistic objects of nature, or with the satisfaction of sensuous passion or by the satisfaction of sense organs. This materialistic world stimulates our gross cravings. Constantly the longing of worldly objects is generated one after another. One sensuous desire is yet to be fulfilled when the next craving is generated. Man collects and hoards boundless riches, seeks pleasure in unrestrained sexual play and cheats others by grabbing and by the selfish means. He makes conspiracy of fraud, cheating and other different kinds of deceitful acts. He resorts to the sensuous joys, intoxications, jealousy, hostility, but never gets the lasting joy and bliss. He wastes his entire life in a sort of mirage. But just reverse his wicked feelings are agitated more. As much as a man considers the joys of life in the outer worldly objects, so much his individual and collective life is full of dissatisfaction, thorny, mournful and miserable, uncontented and entangled one. The Hindu scholars of Truth had come to the conclusion marking this mistake that selfishness and worldly enjoyments are certainly not the source of permanent joy. The centre of our joys is the self-advancement instead of materialistic pleasure-objects. For the internal purity there are prescribed means of different kinds in order. Sacrifice, martyrdom and self-control—these are the means, which help much in the internal purity.

In the Indian culture, there is the rule of strict restraint of the sense organs. He who is capable of restraining his sensuous passions and sense organs, can share the performance of others service. What will he do his own good and good of the public who fails to control his own body, desires, passions, habits etc.,

‘हरन्ति दोषजातानि नरमिन्द्रियकिङ्करम्।’

(Mahabharat)

‘The man who is slave of his sense-organs (and his instincts) is dragged away towards vices.’

‘बलवानिन्द्रियग्रामो विद्वांसमपि कर्षति।’

(Manu. 2/215)

‘The sense-organs are very powerful. They forcibly carry away even the wise towards sense objects.’

So, the Indian culture has always appreciated the strict treatment with ownself.’ If we fail to restrain our vicious tendencies, our energy will be wasted. He is the ideal Indian who follows all these three—(Dam, Dan, Yama) control, donation, yama. Specially, control out of these three—(Dam—means, subjugation of the sense-organs) is the eternal principle of the Indian seers of Truth. Self-restraint increases spiritual lustre and manliness. ‘Dana’ is absolutely pure and superior. By adding and enhancing his powers, man becomes lustrous and free from sin by self-control. Whatever the fruits of divine rules, morality auspicious deeds or the performance of all the Yagyas are, the self-control is more important. The action of donation can not be fully purified without self-control. So, it is the ‘Dama’ only that creates the mentality of ‘Dana’ and ‘Yagya’.

The man who does not control himself by the subjugation of his sense organs and self-control, what is the use of his renunciation and dwelling in the forest? and what is the gain to live in a forest or in any hermitage by taking renunciation for the man who has no control on his sense organs and what is the need of living in the forest or in the hermitage abandoning his house unless he has control over his senses and his mind?

Wherever a man who has controlled his senses lives, the same place is forest and a great hermitage for him. He who is devoted to amiability and good conduct and who has already controlled his sense organs and who lives with simplicity of what avail are hermitages to him? The modifications are caused in the men attached to the sensuousness even in the forests and if the five sense-organs are controlled even a domestic life, is verily the penance.

He who is always engaged in the benevolent or good deeds, for such a detached person his home is the forest of penance. Dwelling alone in the aloofness, following the moral rules strictly and firmly and keeping away his sense organs from the worldly attachments, remains busy in the pondering of spiritual truth is the fruit of Indian culture.

On one side whereas Indian culture preaches the sermon of self-restraint, on the next side insists on to be generous to others more and more. A true Indian should always remain prompt for the service, co-operation and support.

सत्यस्य वचनं श्रेय: सत्यज्ञानं तु दुष्करम््।

यद्‍भूतहितमत्यन्तमेतत् सत्यं ब्रवीम्यहम्॥

(Mahabharat)

Means—‘To speak the truth is the most benedictory, but the knowledge of truth is very difficult. So, I consider the truth simply which is much beneficial for the beings.’

आत्मोत्कर्षं न मार्गेत परेषां परिनिन्दया।

स्वगुणैरेव मार्गेत विप्रकर्षं पृथग् जनात्॥

Means—‘Never see your progress in the censure of others. He is the true Indian who wishes the evolution of other men with his own virtues. The worshipper of Indian culture are always the helpers and supporters of shelter-seeking and weakers.’

In India, there is the tradition of generosity with others. The Indian culture has been generous to even those who came here from the outside to kill them, who gave poison, who burnt in fire, who got trampled with elephants and who got bitten with snakes. We have seen the God in all. We have observed the sight of Vishnu in the elephants, in the serpents, in the water and in the fire also, then, to see God in animals and men is much more valuable. We have been of the generous nation to love all the creatures as a whole.

 

The glory of Gayatri and Cow

Gayatri is the eternal and beginningless of Indian culture. It is mentioned in the Purans—

‘The creator of the universe, Lord Brahma had got this ‘Gayatri Mantra’ through the oracle. He had acquired the power of the creation of this world by the penance of practice of this spell. As the explanation of the four parts of Gayatri, Brahmaji described the Vedas with four faces. Gayatri is called ‘Vedmata’ the mother of Vedas. All the four Vedas are merely the exposition of Gayatri.’

In the 24 letters of Gayatri, the teachings of Vedas, Shastra, Puran, Smriti, Upanisad etc., have been given which can provide man the individual social and spiritual happiness and peace. In the Gita, Lord Shri Krishna has Himself said—‘गायत्री छन्दसामहम्’ It means—‘I Myself, am the ‘Gayatri Mantra’ among the vedic hymns.

Gayatri is the superiormost spell of India, that is why, it is said that it bestows longevity, knowledge, son, glory, wealth and the lustre of the Brahma. By the practice of the worship of Gayatri, all the impurity distraction frozen on our spirit are washed away and the purified form of soul appears and different accomplishments and ocult powers start coming out. Just after the start of Gayatri worship the spiritual power of man increases in his inner-self and the vices are removed away. The quantity of self-restraint, modesty, zeal, smartness, labour, sweetness, honesty, truthfulness, generosity, love, contentment, peace, the spirit of service, close affinity etc., virtues begin to enhance day by day. Gayatri has been called here, the ‘Kamdhenu’ (Cow of plenty, fulfilling all desires) because it satisfies the spiritual hunger and thirst. Gayatri has been called the nectar of the earth also; because it fills us with the power to get the true nectar, having released from the wheel of birth and death. By the worship of Gayatri on the priority basis, the spiritual advancement is made, this is the chief gain. Gayatri is supporter in progressing the direction of self-redemption, happiness and peace.

The mother cow is the shining symbol of Indian culture. The ancient Aryans have said—‘मातेव रक्षति’ means ‘May this mother protect us! The Supreme Lord, Shri Krishna had shown this admirable path by the service of cow, so that we might adopt the ideal in our life. By emphasising the importance of cow mother in the ‘Rigveda’ and ‘Atharv Veda’ many useful sentences of doctorine have been said which are quoted here—

माता रुद्राणां दुहिता वसूनां

स्वसादित्यानाममृतस्य नाभि:।

प्र नु वाचं चिकितुषे जनाय

मा गामनागामदितिं वधिष्ट॥

(Rigved 8/101/15)

Means—‘Cow is the mother of ‘Rudras’ (gods) the daughter of Vasus (demi-gods), the sister of Aditiputras and the treasure of nectar in the form of ghee. It is the duty of every thoughtful man not to kill the cow the innocent and worthy of not to be slain.’

यदि नो गां हंसि यद्यश्वं यदि पूरुषम्।

तं त्वा सीसेन विध्यामो यथा नोऽसो अवीरहा॥

(Atharvaved 1/16/4)

Means—‘If you kill our cow, horse and man, I will bind you with the ball of glass, so that you may not kill my braves.’

यूयं गावो मेदयथा कृशं चिदश्रीरं चित् कृणुथा सुप्रतीकम्।

भद्रं गृहं कृणुथ भद्रवाचो बृहद्वो वय उच्यते सभासु॥

(Atharvaved 4/21/6)

Means—‘O the Cows! You make the man of lean and thin body hale and hearty and make handsome in appearance to the men who are empty of lustre. Not only this, you make our houses auspicious with your auspicious words. That is why, it is only your glory, sung in the gatherings.’

There are numberless gains from the cows. Considering the usefulness of cow, the Hindus have given her such a high status. For an agricultural country like India, the rearing of cow and the protection of cow is religion. The mankind as a whole will always remain indebted to the mother, cow for the numberless benefit to the human beings. The decay of the cow race is harmful for the nation and society from economic and moral both point of views. There should be the increase in efforts—to increase the number of cow-sheds in every village and city, so that the continuity of the sufficient availability of milk, ghee, fertiliser and strong bullocks may be maintained. In India rearing of cows and their protection is the ‘Sanatan Dharma’.

 

The nectar of life

It is the knowledge of life which is the nectar to guide the human life to tread on the life and path free from throne. The man having the more knowledge of life and joy and sorrow, loss and gain, good and bad, sin and virtue, ups and down, proceeds onward leaving others behind and he is acknowledged as successful.

The knowledge of life is achieved by two ways. Man lives his own life. He commits errors of different kinds. He is punished for every error and deserves praise and appreciation for his success. He gets the experience of life on the basis of his pleasure and bitterness. On the basis of this experience he crosses the distress and adverse circumstances. Without experience, the unripe man falls down on every step and gets punishment. That experience is the total sum of life.

But by experience the road of getting wisdom is long and complicated. There are several men who commit mistakes again and again but even then, remain devoid of experience and fail to get its advantage. Those who go ahead only on the basis of their experience, no doubt, get its benefit but that experience is got too late after growing old. Some experiences are got within months and years. Sometimes it causes a great loss which cost is paid throughout the life, A wrong matter has its very harmful effect.

The second type of knowledge is got from the collection in the books, stored and saved from the ages passed and written in an attractive and pleasant style, if we remained dependent on our personal experience got in the life, half of our life may pass in understanding these experiments and useful rules and the ways and means of its practice; because every clue of life is got after a heavy cost.

Life is a big book. In this book each and every day is like one page. Every line gives a new mystery. But the life instead of one or two days, one or two years, is of years long. We come to know all the mysteries when our life reaches the edge of death. Then, the breaths of life don’t remain to practise these experiences conclusions valuable clues and useful rules of life in our life.

So, as soon as possible we get the true experiences of life, useful rules and the matters of benefit, from anywhere, we can form a higher life as soon as we begin to implement them.

Everyone who has written the experience of life, practises them in his life also. He proceeds onward on its basis. He takes its benefit by following which the great men had achieved repute, glory, respect and success.

Every good book is extract of the life

What you consider book is not simply a motionless and lifeless object of paper. Books and monthly magazines are living commotion of life.

There is the divinity of experience in each and every word of the books and news magazines; there is the solution of the hardships of the ways of life, there is the coolness of the tree-shade; there is the undaunted faith and fragrant life; the fragrant flowers of heart are rejoicing and there is the golden source to make the earth heaven. The winter moon of hope is spreading the laughing light in them and the silver beams are scattered.

In the world of the books there are great seers and sages, the great thinkers of the world are there, the poets, writers and leaders are alive in the books. They are always ready to support, they have no consideration of day and night. Whenever and wherever we want, we may avail the company of our those preceptors and friends sitting in the books.

In the pages of books there is a permanently decorated living world. In this mortal world. God knows when this body, a lump of flesh and bones will be perished, but the experiences written there in the books are long undecaying.

In the books there are the methods to solve all the problems of the world. The books are filled with the conclusions of the profound mystries of life and are avaliable to us.

Believe it, the knowledge which you would get after passing fifty years of life, can be achieved by you from the good books in the beginning of life or even today or whenever you like.

There is the presence of scholars, thinkers and saints in the houses where the books are present. You have already kept a number of wise and learned men in your almirah.

In the words of sage Tiruvallavar—‘The men of letters are like fragrant flowers. Wherever they go, they carry with them the sweet fragrant joy. Everywhere they have their dwelling and everywhere their motherland is.’

‘Knowledge is wealth. Other objects are negligible in its comparison. It is such a wealth, that accompanies a man even in the next births, in the generations to generations of the man, in the form of sacraments in the family.

The intelligence, purified by knowledge goes on ascending in the next births gradually and his life going higher reaches the consummate.

As much as well is dug, so much water is got, similarly, as much self-study, learning and teaching is made, so much the man becomes learned and wise.

What is man? What is this world? What is God, this soul and the beings—What happens of the human life after death? How can the best life be passed? These can be known only by them who have studied well seriously the books of the great thinkers, who have learnt knowledge in true sense.

It creates surprise, why the people are lazy in earning such a incomparable wealth?

Age is no bar. Study can be made at any age. A man should remain enthusiastic to get knowledge in any age even when he has become old and lying on death-bed. Knowledge is a divine property to accompany you in the births after births. Only he who is well read, has eyes really. He who has no knowledge is blind. His mind has only two pits but not eyes. It is the knowledge that has eyes.

Your friend might possibly leave your company, but the virtuous association of books is always open to you.

If the useful knowledge, got by self-study is practised in life, you can be escaped from so many foolishnesses of life very easily.

The thoughts, collected in the books have brought so many big revolutions in the world. It is a great mistake to think them dead one. They have great power. They are living as their authors. Just as any very effectual medicine is preserved in a bottle very carefully for the use in life, similarly a good book preserves the sole truth of the great soul-life. From the conclusions of the same life we can take the maximum benefit.

Remember the words of the poet, Milton—

‘A superior book is like the invaluable blood-drops of a great soul, which is eternal in usefulness and good guide. It consists of the best juice, the total sum of experiences for the future generation.’

This human life is quite rare, it is not available again and again. The experiences of this life cannot work in the next new life. It is not known whether this unobtainable life will be got in the next life or not. So, without waiting for our experiences to be ripe, we should take the maximum benefit by the self-study of these books.

You waste your free moments uselessly in cinema, clubs, gossips, gambling, playcards, useless talks and discussions. These means of recreations are not healthy. The means of self-study is healthy and effectual.

Self-study develops your hidden strength and powers and you live in the good company of highly exalted souls. They guide you the new directions to the holy thoughts and imaginations.

Self study should be the part of our daily life. As it has been said also—

सर्वस्य लोचनं शास्त्रम्।

(Hito. pra. 10)

‘Actually, Shastras are the eyes of all.’

विद्या स्फीयते ज्ञानम्।

(Mahabharat)

‘Knowledge develops experience.’

 

The wonderful volume of the world which is never old

The most popular book of the world is—Gita. The lacs of copies of the Gita have been sold and even now, the numberless men of the world read it and consider it the most favourite. The reason behind it is that this small volume consists in brief of the gist of human knowledge, spirituality, ethics, moral duty, Vedas, Shastras. This is the most important conclusion of Mahabharat.

The problems of the world have always been complicated but its clue of solution is found in the Gita. There is only the need of the man who may understand it well countless number of learned men of India and foreign countries, wrote more than fifty commentaries and explanations of the Gita, hundreds of detailed and minute criticisms and comments were written. Gita was translated in a number of languages and thousands of editions were published. Rarely there would be any language in the world, in which the Gita would have not been translated. Even the foreigners have appreciated the Gita and declared it the best volume of Indian Philosophy.

The famous American Philosopher Emerson went to meet the English thinker and essayist, Carlayle—

‘Will you present me any book with your own hands? I want the gift, the most favourite to you and which has inspired you the most’, said Emerson.

Carlayle said—‘You want that gift which has proved to be the best guide of my life, and which has been the source of illumination and inspiration in my life.’

He remained pondering over for a while and remained moving before the almirah of His library fully packed with books, then, presenting a small book he said—

‘Please, take this book, my dearest book.’

Emerson took that book and saw its name—this was the translation of ‘Shrimadbhagavat Gita’ in English.

Carlayle said—‘This is the most favourite gift of India to the world and my dearest gift to you. This book has covered the entire spiritualism of the world, the welfare of human being as a whole and the guideline in all the situations in the form of pithy verses.’

Emerson said—‘This is a very small book.’

Carlayle said—‘Yes, this is the collection of pithy verses. This maxim is the gist of human science, knowledge and spiritualism.’ Well! Nothing more is required. Only this book is sufficient to do good and shape this world and the beautitude as well. Its message can never be old.’

Emerson touched the Gita with his forehead. This gift proved to be the turning point of his life and it gave a new outlook of life. Emerson has written—‘I daily bathe in the holy water of the Gita. Among the books of the present age, the Gita is the foremost. The age when it would have been written, must have been some supernatural age.’

Reading the Gita, the German scholar Shlegal had come to emotion. The spirituality of Gita has its very powerful influence on the thoughts of Shoupenahar and Mejani.

Among the Muslims, the prince of Bukhara was a great lover of spiritualism and higher life. Going beyond the narrowness of the religion, he had studied the Sanskrit language also. He was the first man among the Muslims, who had attracted the Islamic world towards the Gita.

Alberuni had said—‘The Gita is the better gift of knowledge to the world. In this single book the gist of all the sects of the world has been presented.’

It is related to the Moghal age—

The Emperor Akabar was the lover of knowledge. When it came to his knowledge that the ‘Shrimadbhagawat Gita’ is the total sum of Vedic religion, he ordered Faizi to translate Gita in the Persian language. Among the Muslim Emperors, whosoever read it, was charmed. Shikoha named it ‘Sirde Akabar’. This was a favourite book of Akabar. Faizi had written in the introduction of this book—

‘Gita is the source of spiritual bliss to the mankind. This book is the guide of the path leading to truth and is full of countless sermons unfolding the deep secrets of spiritualism. This is the creation of the foremost among men, Vyasji having the topmost knowledge, to guide the mankind about the oneness of all the spirits of the world. If is beyond my speech and pen to praise it.’

Really, this is not the experience of single one but of the many.

All the Upanishads are like the cows, the Gita is the milk of nectar and the milkman is Himself, the Lord Shri Krishna.

If the entire literature of India had been destroyed and merely the Gita had been left safe, even then, it was sufficient to remind the glory of Aryan race to the whole world.

Gita is the symbol of Indian culture. In the Vedic religion, whatever the higher thought, the fundamental truth, view points, the elements of the secret of the uplift of human life, all these are included and are found in the combined form in this gem of books only.

Shrimadbhagavat Gita is the spiritual volume to present the concluding gist of Vedic religion and culture. But in the present situations of the country, the Gita is specially beneficial and useful.

Today in the country, narrowness, small disputes, narrow outlook, the discrimination of colour, caste, class, the discrimination on the basis of religion and indifference to duty, all such mentalities have spreadover. The pit of differences between man to man is expanding fast. The country is disturbed with the mentality of fatalism, inactiveness and gloomy disorder. The entire country is in the condition of a type of cowardiceness and suffering from the inferiority complex.

The country is passing through an old situation of doubt and in decision even worse than the condition of Arjuna in the battlefield before the Mahabharat war had not broken out. ‘Whatever I should fight the war or not? What should be my outlook towards war?

The same philosophy of action and duty in the Gita that had persuaded Arjuna to be ready to fight and at last had made him winner, can make the country march ahead. This message of (Krmayoga) unselfish action given by the Gita only can make the country strong.

There is the message in the Gita to do the duty rising above the petty mentality of loss and gain and expectation.

There is the message of action in the Gita. Integrated with Sattvika and unselfish feelings is necessary. In the world ‘श्रीकृष्णार्पणमस्तु’ ‘Surrender yourself to Shri Krishna is needed.’

‘श्रीकृष्णार्पणमस्तु’ The man who has surrendered himself to God with this feeling considers that all the works are not for him, all are for the God, these are for the protection and stability of the world and that is why these are pleasing to the God. This mentality of the devotee having faith in the Gita, makes his secular actions spiritual.

 

Surrender to the God—The inspiring ideal of Gita

Surrendering himself to the Lord, completely when the man offers his entire mental, intellectual and spiritual powers to the feet of the Lord, the old tendencies or instincts of the man, which were badly attached to the worldly enjoyments, now start rising up towards a new direction from downward to upward, from the materialism to divinity. For the spiritual accomplishments, he comes in contact of the divine powers. The man of self-surrender gets a new life.

Be self-restraint and then offer your all the actions, your powers and your desires to the Lord. Such a man, who has surrendered himself completely, has been successful in the work of the public interest.

To offer the entire self to the Lord, to collect the spiritual powers by becoming the Lord’s part or the servant of God’s servant. This discipline of self-purification has been continuing since the ancient time. In the Gita, the Lord has explained the function of self-purification in the following words—

तमेव शरणं गच्छ सर्वभावेन भारत।

तत्प्रसादात्परां शान्तिं स्थानं प्राप्स्यसि शाश्वतम्॥

(18/62)

‘Take refuge in Him alone, with all your being, Arjuna. By His mere grace you will attain supreme peace and the eternal abode.’

चेतसा सर्वकर्माणि मयि संन्यस्य मत्पर:।

बुद्धियोगमुपाश्रित्य मच्चित्त: सततं भव॥

(18/57)

‘Mentally resigning all your duties to Me and taking recourse to Yoga in the form of even-mindedness, be solely devoted to Me and constantly fix your mind on Me.’

We have nothing as our own. Whatever is, belongs to the Lord. We do nothing for ourselves but do everything for the Lord service—by doing anything with this mentality man gets the power beyond limit. That is why the poet has said truly—

मेरा मुझपै कुछ नहीं, जो कुछ है सब तोर।

तेरा तुझको सौंपते, क्या लागे है मोर॥

‘O God! Nothing is mine. This body and everything belongs to You. May your objects, be used in your service in the form of the service of the world and society and may then be back to you again! What is there mine! It is already offered to You!’

 

Give-up the false notion of hunger

False hunger is that appetite, which is an artificial creation of our mind. That is hot the appetite of our stomach, but the mind remains hungry of different kinds of objects, cravings and necessities. The Brahmins of Mathura are renownsed for false hunger. As it is generally said that without hunger by overeating they were those to fall ill who took bitter medicines, remained on long fast and became well after a great trouble. So, one should remain cautious from false hunger.

The materialism is a type of false hunger. Just as in false hunger, there is a useless temptation and mental dissatisfaction, similarity, in the false hunger of materialism the new way of entertainment, the satisfaction of sexual mentality, desires are worthless and not true. Basically, a man does not need them. Due to ignorance, he feels their need. In its fulfilment, as much as he goes on being attached, so much with the same speed it is inflamed like the ghee in fire.

It is the duty of man being awakened to realize the self. The self-realization provides us the emancipation of the self—

दर्शनं ह्यात्मन: कृत्वा जानीयादात्मगौरवम्।

ज्ञात्वा तु तत्तदात्मानं पूर्णोन्नतिपथं नयेत्॥

Means—‘Let us observe the spirit, let us know the spirit, let us realize its great glory and let us tread on the path of self-evolution.’

We should do such noble and higher deeds that are in harmony with the glory of the great spirit. So, the duty of everyone of us is of great responsibility. Without the spiritual behaviour, our life is like the elephant without an elephant-goad, the elephant may go astray there is none to control that elephant. The spiritualism teaches us the behaviour embodied with the spiritual virtues to others and inspires us for the higher life.

A spiritual man glances the same sight of self-spirit in others which is present in his own self. He goes on pouring down his love, pity, compassion and sympathy on others. The orbit of his close affinity is broad enough which includes in it not only mankind but other creatures too.

Spiritualism creates the real and absolutely pure hunger removing away our false hunger. It burns up all latent desires and generates Sattvika feelings, It initiates us towards purity.

When we give the slogan ‘Leave the false hunger!’ We want to say—‘Give up the needless and worthless artificial needs, desires, sensuous passions. The hunger of undesirable meal, the desire of fine clothes and garments, the hunger of grand houses, the luxurious life, the life of enjoyments, unrestrained powers and rights and the hunger of unlimited wealth—all such types of hunger are needless for your personality. It is improper to get entangled with them. You should remain escaped of the materialistic web of illusion and remain giving up all kinds of false hunger. Be free from false artificial life and practise the simple behaviour of simplicity.

The false hunger is unnecessary craving and greed. So, to remain away and maintain distance from it is the only means of a successful life. It is only spiritualism that can remove it.

 

The bliss of heaven and salvation can be experienced here

‘Yoga’, among six parts of Indian philosophy is a great contribution of Hindus and Indian to the world. This is quite different from the other dry thoughts of the world; because it is practical. Yoga is science in itself. If we want, we can name it ‘Eastern Psychology’ also. Those, taking interest in Indian culture give due importance to ‘Yoga’ and see it with respectful sight; because, it is full of spiritual miracles. It was the seer Patanjali to originate the Yoga. According to him, ‘Yoga’ is such a knowledge, where a man can merge himself in God by the control of mind.

The word ‘Yoga’ means ‘Union’ or to unite. How pleasant is the union of two separated persons? By the mutual joining with one another we become firm and strong. We feel the internal exhilaration. Our soul feels joy. Whatever the immaculate, enlightened, consciousness, sentiment, Bliss, beauty, joy, benevolence, undecaying immortal is there in the innerself of man, is the spirit. This spirit is closely related to the eternal, the substratum of all Supreme fundamental truth, the Supreme, Lord. By the means of Yoga, when this spirit unites with Supreme Spirit, we are overwhelmed with that joyous sentiment and feeling like the mental condition of the child depending on the mother’s milk, when meets her after separation. Really that joy has no simile.

The feeling created after the union with the Lord is to give unlimited joy and eternal peace. The joy got by the devotee by the Lord’s worship and ultimately union with Him is indescribable.

‘Yoga’ is that knowledge which provides us the joy of the heaven and salvation here in this world. A number of devotees shun their materialistic properties and absorb themselves in the spiritual disciplines (Yama-Niyam, Dhyan, Dharana etc.); because they give more priority to the spiritual bliss than the worldly joys. The realized souls have written their feelings of their union with the Supreme soul. So, it is necessary for the inquisitives to know and experience the miracles of Yoga to study and understand well the knowledge of Yoga with the company of great souls and learneds. Now-a-days, only to perform ‘Asana’ and ‘Pranayam’ is considered complete ‘Yoga’, but these are the sub-ordinate practices of Yoga, only for health purposes, but in real sense it is union with God through mind and soul. For the study of the science of Yoga, zeal, the attainment of virtues and long practice and the virtuous preceptor—these requirements are necessary for the practice of ‘Yoga’.

There are several forms of Yogas as ‘Karmyoga’, ‘Gyanyoga’, ‘Bhaktiyoga’ and ‘Rajyoga’. ‘Yama-Niyama’ are the base without which none can be inclined to the path of ‘Yoga’. The Yogi Shri Arvind has emphasised more on ‘Self-dedication’.

What is the practice of ‘Yoga’? In the inner-self of man, that what is the immaculate, enlightened and consciousness (Shuddha, Buddha, Chaitanya), is immortal reality God, the ‘Spirit’ mind, intellect mind, ego, all these four attached with consciousness is called embodied being. This is also apart from the Lord also not apart. It can be called as ‘Dualism’ (Dvait) and ‘Non-duality’ (Advaita) also. It is the fire that brings forth spark. The spark can be called separate from the fire; but without fire the spark is of no existence, so, this is also the part of fire, which is non-dual. The eternal Supreme Truth is fire and the soul is spark. Both are apart also and the same also. In the ‘Upanishads’, they have been compared with the two birds sitting on the same branch of tree. In the Gita accepting the existence of the both one has been called ‘perishable’ and the second ‘non-perishable’.

Due to misunderstanding, ignorance or illusion the both (The embodied soul and God) become separate from their eternal unity. This is the cause of sorrow and lamentation.

Where the embodied soul and Supreme soul are united, there, the will, inclination and the mode of action of the embodied soul all become according to the will, interest and mode of action of the Supreme soul, then there is the spontaneous overflow of immense, divine joy. In the absence of the spiritual unity, the man’s mental world remains badly disturbed and unpeaceful. The anguish of this disorder of his inner-self world remains blazing like conflagration. The materialistic means of comforts and enjoyments may be even boundless, but his inner-self remains deprived of even the least peace of mind. The master of boundless riches, the seth, capitalists, big officers remain surrounded with different worries, anxieties and anguished. It makes it clear that a man can never get the real and permanent joy or comfort of life by his property, wealth or rights and powers.

In the same way, there are several such men also who are empty of pelf and power and the material opulence and comforts, yet they are free from tension and they lead a carefree life. They enjoy the sound sleep of comfort and remain pleased to see the joy all around them. it makes clear that the scarcity of pelf and power and other worldly facilities does not become the cause of their lessening of joy. The worry of the rich and the happiness of the poors is its evidence that the happiness does not exist in the outwardly objects and the base of the happiness is not external.

In the spiritual unity, there is pleasure in the union of the both. The same can be said in the Yogic philosophy as the union of soul with the eternal Supreme Spirit. The next name of this union is ‘Yoga’. By the union of soul and the Supreme eternal truth and with the combined force of unity such a bliss is originated which is incomparable to any joy of the world. The same bliss is given the different names as Supreme bliss, deliverance of the soul, Brahma who is all peace, spiritual accomplishment the sight of the Lord, etc.

Basically, there is no existence of man’s mind. This is merely and instrument of the soul. There is the existence of mind only to activate the soul’s mode of action in order and by its performance to give the gross form. Its actual function is to adopt the viewpoint, thought and mode of action according to the will and interest of the soul. If the mind functions according to the proper and natural way, the human being takes the real taste of the happy life. But it is unfortunate that most of us are today devoid of this situation. The spirit is mainly the element of truth. Its will and interest is towards purity. The demand of spirit is to find the every moment of life overwhelmed with purity and every thought and action to be endowed with purity.

But being entangled into the web of illuson and ignorance. We are misdirected. Our mind runs after gloom and passion. By the constant encouragement to this mode of action, it becomes so mighty, that the desire and temptation of the mind gets its priority in the place of the call of soul.

After getting rid of this vicious mental tendency following the soul only we can get the real joy. This mode of action is called the Practice of ‘Yoga’. This practice of ‘Yoga’ should be the duty of daily routine for the striver of high properties. According to the Indian culture, the base of real joy and peace is merely the practice of Yoga. When by the means of ‘Yoga’, the man, distressed by the struggles of the world being introvert sits near the soul, he feels the boundless peace.

The above lines throw some light on the importance of Indian ‘Yoga-system’. The ‘Yoga’ is the psychology of eastern view. According to this, a man should attain cravings in the Supreme eternal free from all the a state of stable existence. Contrary to it the Western psychology speaks that there should no restrain on the sensuous passion. This ‘Yoga’ system of Indian Psychology is superior and better; because by this method man’s interest and mental attitude remains higher. The purify and divinity gets sufficient opportunity to develop. The first advantage of the practice of Yoga is the purity of mind and the second advantage is the concentration of mind and peace. By the constant pondering and meditation develops the concentration of mind. The spiritual forces develop. All the modern methods of Western psychology as Psychotherepy, mesmerism, thought reading, clair-voyance etc., are possible through Yoga.

The a great need of the present is to sharpen the right outlook of ‘Yoga’—knowledge. The performance of ‘Asan’ and ‘Pranayam’ have become the entire ‘Yoga’. But the ‘inner-practice’ is more important in real sense. At the time of ‘Yoga’ the Yogis wear the skin of deer so because they used to get it available from the dead deer easily. Now-a-days, the skin of animals shot dead with the bullets of guns are available which is at all condemnable. Now there is no need of tongs The simple life like foremost ascetic, Arvind, Swami Dayanandji, Swami Shivanandji is appropriate at all.

 

The base of real happiness and peace is this

‘Spiritualism’ is the view of theists while ‘materialism’ is the view of atheists. Spiritualism is related to the intutive perceptrion which, is not visible with the physical eyes, but its influence is pervasive and lasting. The spiritualist has integral faith in God. Contrary to it the materalist runs towards the object, which is visible with the physical eyes and which provides instant gain. The modern age is in illusion of worthless concept to earn more, enjoy more and expand your needs and searching for the happiness at the tragic places. His property has expanded; the boundless wealth is there in the countries like America. There is no happiness in wealth, there is dissatisfaction and mirage. There is no lack of energy in the world, varied objects of luxury and comforts are ready but there is not the least satisfaction and peace.

So long as any man or any nation does not has faith in God, he does not get the base of lasting and stable thought. Spiritualism provides us the strong base. Whatever the work a spiritualist takes in his hand, that work is fulfilled automatically with the divine power. The materialist wants to fulfil the work with the worldly efforts, but these works fail to give satisfaction and peace despite of being completed. The materialist looks for the gain which means good for nothing and he dies in the same. That poor does not have such a farsightedness that he may know at least that the worldly objects may vanish in a moment.

Why is the modern world dissatisfied? The reason behind is that the base of his thinking, understanding living and stability is temporary and momentary. If he may adopt spiritualism, he can get energy and peace.

The man, possessing twenty-six qualities of divine property can be called a spiritual man. These qualities are—Absolute fearlessness, perfect purity of mind, constant fixity in the Yoga of meditation for the sake of Self-realization, and even so, charity in its Sattvika form, control of the senses, worship of God and other deities as well as of one’s elders including the performance of Agnihotra (pouring oblations into the sacred fire) and other sacred duties, study and teaching of the Vedas and other sacred books as well as the chanting of God’s names and glories, suffering hardships for the discharge of one’s sacred obligations and uprightness of mind as well as of the body and senses. Non-violence in thought, word and deed, truthfulness and geniality of speech, absence of anger even on provocation, disclaiming doership in respect of actions, quietude or composure of mind, abstaining from slander, compassion towards all creatures, absence of attachment to the objects of senses even during their contact with the senses, mildness, a sense of shame in transgressing the scriptures or social conventions, and abstaining from frivolous pursuits; Sublimity, forgiveness, fortitude, external purity, bearing enmity to none and absence of self-esteem—these are, O Arjun, the marks of him, who is born with the divine endowments.

Contrary to it the materialistic men have the demonic traits. They are hypocrite They say something and do otherwise. Their hypocrisy is markable at every step. It is a matter of great regret that now, those who boast of being spiritualist, are mostly devoid of the qualities of divine property. They are arrogant. They don’t bow down before anybody. They remain overpowered with pride. According to the three qualities—(Sattva, Rajas, Tamas) there can be three states of pride also. All these kinds of proud are to be given up. Such men who have wrath, hard-hearted and ignorance are found in general now-a-days and actually, they are the root cause of disturbance.

Theism teaches us faith in the God. We should not consider the God as the human being of this world having four hands and fourlegs. God is the absolute fundamental truth. As the air is an element. The sceintists have divided the air into many sub-parts—Oxygen, Nytrogen etc., and every part will be called ‘Air’ basically. Similarily, a single essence, which is pervading everywhere, which exists in the innerself of everyone and which interpenetrate all, is Supreme Lord. That spirit is everywhere, all pervading. Spiritual truth is the greatest achievement of our saints and seers. This essence has three forms—

1. The creator, 2. the sustainer, 3. the destroyer. All three powers are prevalent by three names in Indian culture—Brahma, Vishnu and Mahesh. All these three are apparant. None can deny them.

Today, we are in a great need of spiritualism. The enjoyment can not pacify the lust of the enjoyment of worldly objects rather than it intensifies more. It is only the feeling of sacrifice and self-restraint that purifies our mind and the wit is purified by knowledge. It is only the master of his senses who can get salvation. The man attached to worldly objects faces evil destiny.

Self-discipline is better than the control thrust upon by others. Our soul’s voice can inspire us to the path of truth. The earth exists unmoved only because of truth. It is only truth why the sun is blazing and only due to the existence of truth the air is in motion. Everything is constant due to truth only. We should remain always prompt to hold on truth and give up vices.

This human life is not meant for the momentary enjoyment of the sensual objects. The sole duty and the sole purpose of human life is self-realization.

 

Yes, my age is not eighty, only four years

The king Nausherva was going somewhere. He remained fond of knowing any new thing by having conversation with others. By chance, on the way, a white bearded man met him. The old man was of religious mind. Both of them came close to each other. Now the course of discussion started.

Now, the question arose what should be the subject of discussion? Whether politics, arms and weapons, religion, philosophy—ultimately what should be the subject in talk, what subject will interest this old man?

In the course of thinking, the king, Nausherva asked the old man to start the converstation—‘O the old gentle man! What is your age?’

The old man was old enough with completely white hair, mouth toothless, wrinkled face, the eyes were down in pit. His waist was bent, the body limbs were shaking and body shivering! The old remained silent for sometime. Then, he answered seriously—

‘Sir, I am only four years old.’

This answer was somewhat strange. This old man, at the edge of death and his age simply four years! What a wonderful version! What a white lie! It could never be believed. The king got furiated but suppressing his anger, said with showy respect—

‘In this old age such a lie! Bare Minya! Why are you assuming air? Your this exhausted condition, your shaking body, these white hair like milk, are clearly certifying your age not less than eighty years in any condition. Don’t place a riddle. Tell how far I am true in my presumption? My presumption about age can never be wrong as I think.

The old man was looking somewhat astonished and afraid. He was unable to speak any word for a while. He could not make the answer clear.

The king again asked—‘Repeat your words again, I could not really understand.’

Now, the old man became a bit hot and said with the motive to make himself clear—‘Sir, I speak the truth. Really, I am only four years old.’

Now, the king became serious and began to think—‘His words seems to be some what profound.’

Said—‘Bare Miyan! Make your words clear.’

The old man said—‘Sir, your presumption is not wrong. Really the matter is so, that I have wasted seventy-six years uselessly.’

‘Have wasted!’ How can it be possible so? Have you not fed yourself and your family?’

‘Sir, I have wasted these 76 years only in doing such works. I caused the children born. Then, I remained engaged in bringing them up, then supporting them to get any job and getting them married. I remained in the false notion of realizing my main duty to nourish my children and myself till the aged 76 and I did nothing else.’

The king said—‘Then how do you say these years to be wasted?’

‘I do consider them wasted. In this long duration of life, I earned neither any virtue nor helped any poor nor did any work of welfare. I remained living the life of a beast. My valuable time passed away in eating and drinking.

‘For the last four years, I have come to realize that in this long and broad world where as there are living numberless distressed men and pitable creatures, we are not born only for self-gratification but the others have also their right on us. It is our duty to do some good to them, offer our services to them and do some works of welfare.’ By the means of our knowledge or capital, power or intelligences, by our mind and body we have to lift them up and give them some support to progress ahead. The superiority of a man is there when he keeps his family limited and remains satisfied with limited resources and when he takes the benefit of self satisfaction and self happiness by helping and supporting others also who are in great distress, scarcity trouble and depressed. To express pleasure in the happiness of others and offer whole-hearted greetings and wishes to them is one of the most important part of social traits. The civilization and literatures also ordain it that the man is born to do good to others. He should always help and serve to the best of his capacity to those inferior to them, destitutes, helpless, weak, patients, running in scarcity, disappointed persons. This sense has prevailed in me for the last four years. So, I consider my real age as four years only.’

Hearing these words of the old man, Nausherwa became thoughtful. He realized that he himself is also guilty from this point of view and he had also not started yet to live in real sense.

A man may be at the top of richness, health, learning, well off and satisfaction, but all these can provide him only the materialistic means and comforts. He can fulfil his own interest as well as the family interest, This sphere is very limited. All animals seek their own welfare and welfare of their family but that is not the man’s human life. To produce more children and pass the whole life only in bringing up and feeding them is not a better life than an animal-life.

It is not the sign of prudence to use the entire competence and talent only in earning and spending in own interest. If we continue sacrificing in the public interest and in the service of the people and the world being for their moral uplift, shaping ourselves pious more and more. We can create a heaven on this earth—

यस्तु सर्वाणि भूतान्यात्मन्येवानुपश्यति।

सर्वभूतेषु चात्मानं ततो न विजुगुप्सते॥

(Rigved 40/6)

It means—‘He who considers the sorrow-joy and loss-gain of all the beings with such an angle as if his own sorrow and joy, gets rid of all the suspicions and doubts. He serves all the beings perceiving God in all. Really, his life is blessed and praise-worthy who works for the uplift of the society taking it the form of the Almighty God.’
